HD         UPDATE 3-Philips  names Asia background cost-cutter new CFO WC        683 words
PD         29 November 2010
ET          09:40 AM
SN         Reuters News
SC         LBA
LA          English
CY         (c) 2010 Reuters Limited

LP
* Healthcare CFO Ron Wirahadiraksa takes over on March 31
* Healthcare unit cut jobs in 2008-2009 under Wirahadiraksa

TD
* LG.Philips  fined for price fixing  when Wirahadiraksa CFO
* Current CFO going, new appointment surprises analysts
* Shares down 3.9 percent vs 2 percent fall of AEX index
(Adds LG.Philips price  fixing;  Philips, analyst comment; updates shares) By Gilbert Kreijger
AMSTERDAM, Nov 29 (Reuters) - Philips named a healthcare executive with extensive Asian and restructuring experience as its new chief financial officer in a surprise move that gives Philips a new top duo to revamp its consumer unit.
Ron Wirahadiraksa, 50, a Dutch-Indonesian who spent several years working at a Philips' business in
South Korea, has been CFO at Philips' healthcare unit since 2008.

During that time, healthcare and other Philips' divisions cut several thousand jobs in response to the global economic downturn in 2008-2009, and analysts expect further restructuring, including the sale of television and other consumer businesses.

Wirahadiraksa's appointment marks the second senior management change in the company in recent months and highlights the growing emphasis on the healthcare division at Philips, which is the world's third-largest hospital equipment maker after U.S.-listed General Electric and Germany's Siemens. Restructuring expert Frans van Houten will take over as chief executive at Philips on April 1.
Wirahadiraksa, a Dutch citizen with Indonesian roots, will take on the job as group CFO from March 31. South Korea's LG.Philips  LCD, now LG Display and where Wirahadiraksa was CFO from 1999-2008
plead guilty two years ago to a global price fixing  scheme between 2001 and 2006 in a U.S. Justice
Department case and paid $400 million in fines.
The European Commission also started an investigation in 2006 into suspected price-fixing  on LCD
panels.

"This case involves LG.Philips  LCD and not Philips. The appointment of Mr. Wirahadiraksa as CFO is clearly a signal of the company's confidence in him," a Philips spokesman said.

Philips shares ended down 3.9 percent at 21.175 euros by 1616 GMT, lagging an Amsterdam blue chip index which was down 2 percent.
CONSUMER ELECTRONICS


Page 4 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
The Dutch company has been struggling with sluggish sales at its consumer electronics unit, which
sells toasters, shavers and TVs, and there has been talk it may have to abandon its three-pillar strategy
-- of healthcare, consumer electronics and lighting -- given the limited synergies.

"The shortfall in revenue growth that Philips had to report in the second half of this year is an eye opener, as it shows that consumer electronics is still a problem area," SNS Securities analyst Victor Bareno said in a note ahead of Philips' investor day on consumer products on Dec. 1. "We expect this will trigger Philips to accelerate the exit strategy for these activities," Bareno said.

ING analyst Sjoerd Ummels said he expected Philips, which has already been outsourcing some TV production operations, to focus its consumer products on healthcare and personal care but did not think Philips would be breaking up soon.

"There is investor pressure for operational improvement and growth. This is what new management will have to realise. If this does not materialise in two years' time, shareholder pressure will rise," Ummels said.

Wirahadiraksa, who started at Philips in 1987, could help Philips grow in Asia thanks to his experience in the region and his Indonesian background, Ummels said.
Wirahadiraksa helped lead the initial public offering of LG.Philips  LCD on the Korean and New York
Stock exchanges in 2004, Philips said in a statement.

Philips said the resignation of current CFO, Pierre-Jean Sivignon, whose term was until 2013, was for personal reasons and he would pursue his career outside the firm.
The news surprised outsiders.

"As a company you don't want your CEO and CFO to leave at the same time. That is bad planning," Jos Versteeg, analyst at Theodoor Gilissen, said. (Reporting by Gilbert Kreijger; Editing by Matthew Jones and Karen Foster)

HD          UPDATE 1-LG Display, 4 others face EU antitrust fines-sources
WC         353 words
PD          29 November 2010
ET           06:16 PM
SN          Reuters News
SC          LBA
LA           English
CY          (c) 2010 Reuters Limited

LP
* Fines seen for AU Optronics Corp, Chunghwa Picture Tubes
* Chi Mei Optoelectronics, HannStar also due to be  fined

TD
* No fine for Samsung Electronics, alerted  EU Commission
* U.S. probe of sector led to criminal  fines above $890 mln
By Foo Yun Chee

BRUSSELS, Nov 29 (Reuters) - Five companies, including LG Display and Taiwanese group AU Optronics are set to be  fined by EU antitrust regulators next week for  fixing  prices of display panels used in consumer devices, four sources said on Tuesday.

The European Commission, which handles EU regulatory affairs, charged the companies in July last year with breaching EU laws on restrictive business practices. Several other regulators around the world also investigated the sector.
The Commission was expected to unveil the  fines on Dec. 8, one of the sources said.

The EU watchdog did not identify the companies at the time, but LG Display, the world No. 2  LCD maker, global No. 3 AU, and Chi Mei Optoelectronics Corp, Taiwan's second-largest  LCD firm, confirmed the charges.
A Commission document obtained by Reuters showed the companies on the charge sheet included
Chunghwa Picture Tubes, Taiwan's third-largest LCD maker, and HannStar Display Corp. World No.1
LCD maker Samsung Electronics will not be fined, as it alerted the Commission to the  cartel, another
source said.

Dutch company Philips received a copy of the charge sheet as a former shareholder of LG Display, but said it was not directly involved. It sold the rest of its shares in the joint venture with LG Electronics in March 2009.

In a similar investigation by the U.S. Department of Justice, eight companies including LG Display, Chi Mei, Chunghwa, Japanese company Sharp Corp and Hitachi Displays, paid more than $890 million in criminal fines for price-fixing.

The Commission's case had centred on thin-film liquid crystal display panels used in computers, mobile phones, televisions, digital watches, pocket calculators and MP3 players. (Editing by Rex Merrifield and Dan Lalor)

BRUSSELS -- Five companies, including LG Display and Taiwanese group AU Optronics are set to be fined by EU antitrust regulators next week for  fixing  prices of display panels used in consumer devices, four sources said on Tuesday.

The European Commission, which handles EU regulatory affairs, charged the companies in July last year with breaching EU laws on restrictive business practices. Several other regulators around the world also investigated the sector.

TD
The Commission was expected to unveil the  fines on Dec. 8, one of the sources said.

The EU watchdog did not identify the companies at the time, but LG Display, the world No. 2  LCD maker, global No. 3 AU, and Chi Mei Optoelectronics Corp, Taiwan's second-largest  LCD firm, confirmed the charges.
A Commission document obtained by Reuters showed the companies on the charge sheet included
Chunghwa Picture Tubes, Taiwan's third-largest LCD maker, and HannStar Display Corp. World
No. 1 LCD maker Samsung Electronics will not be fined, as it alerted the Commission to the  cartel,
another source said.

Dutch company Philips received a copy of the charge sheet as a former shareholder of LG Display, but said it was not directly involved. It sold the rest of its shares in the joint venture with LG Electronics in March 2009.

In a similar investigation by the U.S. Department of Justice, eight companies including LG Display, Chi Mei, Chunghwa, Japanese company Sharp Corp. and Hitachi Displays, paid more than $890 million (U.S.) in criminal  fines for price-fixing.

The Commission's case had centred on thin-film liquid crystal display panels used in computers, mobile phones, televisions, digital watches, pocket calculators and MP3 players.

Page 10 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.


HD      ELECTRONICS : FINES LIKELY FOR LCD SCREEN CARTEL WC     248 words
PD      6 December 2010
SN      Europolitics SC      EURREP VOL    4097
LA      English
CY      Copyright 2010 Europe Information Service All Rights Reserved

LP
Following an investigation opened last July on the basis of a number of complaints for price-fixing arrangements on LCD flat screens, the  European Commission is expected to issue a verdict soon against five companies. A source close to the inquiry notes that the measure against the  cartel will be announced on 8 December.

The cartel concerns liquid crystal display (LCD) screens used in television sets, as computer screens and in mobile phone, MP3 players and video cameras.

TD
Although the EU executive has not published the participants' names, the world's second and third largest manufacturers, LG Display and AU Optronics Corp, respectively, plus Chi Mei Optoelectronics, number two in Taiwan, have acknowledged that they are among the suspected firms.

World leader Samsung Electronics, which blew the whistle and recognised its participation in illegal practices with fellow manufacturers, could be given total immunity.

LG, under investigation in Japan and South Korea, was already  fined US$400 million in 2009 in the United States for concerted practices on these same products. An anti-trust case was also opened last August against a number of firms, including Hitachi, LG, Toshiba, Samsung, Sharp, AU Optronics and Chi Mei, suspected of  fixing  prices for their screens and rates charged to computer manufacturers. High compensation could be ordered to make up for the "hundreds of millions of dollars" that counties, schools and cities in the State of New York have spent on overpriced  LCD screens.

HD         UPDATE 1-LG Display, Chi Mei, others face EU fines-source
WC         467 words
PD          6 December 2010
ET          03:34 PM
SN          Reuters News
SC          LBA
LA          English
CY          (c) 2010 Reuters Limited

LP
* Biggest penalty for Chi Mei Optoelectronics
* Fines seen for AU Optronics Corp, Chunghwa Picture Tubes

TD
* HannStar also due to be  fined
* No fine for Samsung Electronics, alerted  EU Commission
* U.S. probe of sector led to criminal  fines above $890 mln
(Adds details, background) By Foo Yun Chee
BRUSSELS, Dec 6 (Reuters) - EU regulators are set to  fine LG Display , Chi Mei Optoelectronics Corp and three other firms up to 700 million euros ($928 million) in total for  fixing  prices of display panels used in consumer devices, a source close to the case said on Monday.

The European Commission, the EU antitrust watchdog, charged the companies in July last year with breaching EU laws on restrictive business practices, while other regulators around the world have also investigated the sector.
"The total  fine will be between 600 and 700 million euros," the source told Reuters.

The EU executive will levy the biggest  fine on Taiwan's Chi Mei, the source said, declining to provide details of the individual  fines.

Chi Mei paid $220 million in  fines last year after pleading guilty to U.S. charges of price-fixing.  The company later merged to form Chi Mei Innolux , a combination which now comprises Taiwan's largest maker of LCD panels.

The Commission is expected to announce its decision on Wednesday, sources told Reuters previously. [ID:nLDE6AS238]
The Commission can penalise companies up to 10 percent of their global turnover for infringing EU
laws.

The watchdog did not identify the companies at the time, but LG Display, 3 AU Optronics and Chi Mei confirmed the charges.

Taiwanese firms Chunghwa Picture Tubes and HannStar Display Corp were also named in a Commission document obtained by Reuters. World No.1  LCD maker Samsung Electronics will not be fined as it alerted the Commission to the  cartel.

Dutch company Philips received a copy of the charge sheet as a former shareholder of LG Display, but said it was not directly involved. It sold the rest of its shares in the joint venture with LG Electronics in March 2009.

Page 12 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
The EU Commission's case had centred on thin-film liquid crystal display panels used in computers, mobile phones, televisions, digital watches, pocket calculators and MP3 players.

In the U.S. Department of Justice investigation, eight companies, including LG Display, Chi Mei, Chunghwa, Japanese company Sharp Corp and Hitachi Displays, paid more than $890 million in criminal fines for price-fixing.

Japan's Fair Trade Commission slapped  fines on Sharp Corp and Hitachi Ltd in 2008 for price  fixing  in the market for  LCD panels. (Editing by Rex Merrifield and David Holmes) ($1=.7541 Euro)

HD      EU slaps 649 million euro fine on Asian flat-screen cartel
WC     96 words
PD      8 December 2010
ET       01:11 PM
SN      Agence France Presse
SC      AFPR
LA       English
CY      Copyright Agence France-Presse, 2010 All reproduction and presentation rights reserved.

LP
The European Commission on Wednesday announced 649 million euros in  fines against South Korean and Taiwanese makers of LCD flat screens for running an illegal  cartel that fixed prices.
Taiwan's AU Optronics, Chimei InnoLux Corporation, Chunghwa Picture Tubes and HannStar Display
Corporation were hit with  fines along with South Korean firm LG Display.

TD
South Korea's Samsung Electronics was also accused for being part of the  cartel but avoided a fine for being the first to provide information on the alleged scheme.

HD      EU slaps 649 million euro fine on Asian flat-screen cartel
WC     311 words
PD      8 December 2010
ET       01:43 PM
SN      Agence France Presse
SC      AFPR
LA       English
CY      Copyright Agence France-Presse, 2010 All reproduction and presentation rights reserved.

LP
The European Commission imposed on Wednesday 649 million euros (860 million dollars) in fines
against South Korean and Taiwanese makers of  LCD flat screens for running a price-fixing  cartel.
Taiwan's AU Optronics, Chimei InnoLux Corporation, Chunghwa Picture Tubes and HannStar Display
Corporation were hit with  fines along with South Korean firm LG Display.

TD
South Korea's Samsung Electronics was also accused for being part of the  cartel but avoided a fine for being the first to provide information on the alleged scheme.

Europe's competition watchdog accused the firms of running a  cartel between October 2001 and February 2006 that fixed prices, harming European buyers of televisions and computers equipped with the liquid crystal display component.

The companies held monthly meetings to agree on price ranges and minimum prices, and trade information on future production planning, capacity utilisation, pricing and other commercial conditions, the commission said.

Company officials met 60 times, mainly in hotels in Taiwan, for what they dubbed "the Crystal meetings," the regulator said.

The investigation found that the companies knew they were breaking competition rules and took steps to conceal their meetings.

The commission cited a document urging everybody "to take care of security/confidentiality matters and to limit written communication."

Chimei InnoLux was given the largest  fine, 300 million euros, followed by 215 million euros against LG Display.

AU Optronics was  fined 116.8 million euros, followed by nine million euros for Chunghwa Picture Tubes and 8.1 million euros for HannStar Display.

"Foreign companies, like European ones, need to understand that if they want to do business in Europe they must play fair," European competition commissioner Joaquin Almunia said in a statement.

"The companies concerned knew they were breaking competition rules and took steps to conceal their illegal behaviour," he said.

Page 18 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.


HD      EU slaps huge fine on South Korea, Taiwan LCD cartel
WC     534 words
PD      8 December 2010
ET       04:37 PM
SN      Agence France Presse
SC      AFPR
LA       English
CY      Copyright Agence France-Presse, 2010 All reproduction and presentation rights reserved.

LP
The European Commission imposed Wednesday 649 million euros in  fines on South Korean and Taiwanese electronics firms for secret backroom price-fixing  of LCD flat screens for Europe's TVs and computers.

The fines, worth 860 million dollars, were slapped on Taiwan's AU Optronics, Chimei InnoLux Corporation, Chunghwa Picture Tubes and HannStar Display Corporation along with South Korean firm LG Display.

TD
The leader in the  LCD business, South Korea's Samsung Electronics, was also accused of being part of the cartel but escaped cash sanctions for coming forward first with information on the alleged scheme.

"Foreign companies, like European ones, need to understand that if they want to do business in Europe they must play fair," European competition commissioner Joaquin Almunia said in a statement.

"The companies concerned knew they were breaking competition rules and took steps to conceal their illegal behaviour," he said.

Europe's competition watchdog accused the firms of running a  cartel between October 2001 and February 2006 that fixed prices, harming European buyers of televisions and computers equipped with liquid crystal displays.

The companies held monthly meetings to agree on price ranges and minimum prices, and traded information on future production planning, capacity utilisation, pricing and other commercial conditions, the commission said.

Company officials met 60 times, mainly in hotels in Taiwan, for what they dubbed "the Crystal meetings," the regulator said.

"The fact that the  cartel meetings took place outside the EU is no excuse," Almunia told a news conference, saying the group was "very well organised."

The investigation found that the companies knew they were breaking competition rules and took steps to conceal their meetings.

The commission cited a document urging everybody "to take care of security/confidentiality matters and to limit written communication."

Chimei InnoLux faces the largest  fine, 300 million euros, followed by 215 million euros against LG Display.

AU Optronics was  fined 116.8 million euros, followed by nine million euros for Chunghwa Picture Tubes and 8.1 million euros for HannStar Display.

The cartel's scheme had a direct impact on European consumers because "the vast majority" of televisions, computer monitors and electronic notebooks with  LCD panels that are sold in Europe come from Asia, the commission said.

The market was worth more than seven billion euros over the period that the  cartel existed.
Page 19 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
The European Commission opened its investigation in late 2006 at the same time as other competition regulators in the United States and Asia.
In July 2009, Brussels sent a list of complaints to several companies, including Samsung and LG and
Japanese firms Sharp, Seiko Epson, Toshiba Matsushita and NEC.
The commission did not  fine any Japanese company on Wednesday.

Almunia said the  fines involved activities related to flat screens for TVs, computers and notebooks -- areas in which the Japanese firms were not involved.

LG and Chunghwa, along with Sharp, pleaded guilty in the United States and were  fined a total of 585 million dollars in November 2008. LG was hit with the harshest penalty, 400 million dollars.

The European Commission cracked down on seven cartels this year, imposing nearly three billion euros in total fines.

Page 20 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.


HD     EU fines LCD panel makers euro649 million ($857 million) for cartel, Samsung escapes fine
WC    361 words
PD     8 December 2010
ET      03:37 PM
SN     Associated Press Newswires
SC     APRS
LA      English
CY     (c) 2010. The Associated Press. All Rights Reserved.

LP
BRUSSELS (AP) - The EU competition watchdog  fined five Taiwanese and South Korean electronics companies euro649 million ($857 million) Wednesday for  fixing  prices on LCD panels between 2001 and
2006.
A sixth company, Samsung Electronics Co., also participated in the price  fixing  but escaped a fine
because it blew the whistle on the  cartel, the European Commission said.

TD
Chimei InnoLux Corp. received the biggest  fine, euro300 million ($396 million), LG Display Co. has to pay euro215 million ($284 million), while AU Optronics Corp. was  fined euro116.8 million ($154 million). Two smaller companies, Chunghwa Picture Tubes Ltd. and HannStar Display Corp., received  fines of euro9 million ($11.9 million) and euro8.1 million ($10.7 million) respectively.

Monday's fines targeted price-fixing  for LCD panels used in flat screens for televisions, computer monitors and electronic notebooks. The European Union's initial investigation had also included smaller LCD screens like the ones built into mobile phones, digital cameras, or MP3 players, but the  fines did not target price-fixing  for those products.
"This was a very well organized  cartel," said Competition Commissioner Joaquin Almunia.

Between Oct. 2001 and Feb. 2006, the companies met about 60 times, mostly in Taiwanese hotels, for what they called "the Crystal meetings," the Commission said. In addition to  fixing  prices, they also exchanged information on their future production plans and other business plans, it said.

The cartel affected LCD panel sales worth about euro7 billion ($9.24 billion) in the European market, Almunia said, and the cartel's impact on consumers was strong because most televisions and computers sold in the region come from Asia.

"Foreign companies, like European ones, need to understand that if they want to do business in Europe they must play fair," said Almunia. "The companies concerned knew they were breaking competition rules and took steps to conceal their illegal behavior."
The European Commission launched the cartel investigation in 2006 in parallel with similar action by
U.S. regulators. These followed probes by South Korea and Japan.
None of the companies could be reached for comment Wednesday afternoon.

HD     A look at economic developments and activity in major stock markets around the world
WC    1,213 words
PD     8 December 2010
ET      09:32 PM
SN     Associated Press Newswires
SC     APRS
LA      English
CY     (c) 2010. The Associated Press. All Rights Reserved.

LP
A look at economic developments and activity in major stock markets around the world Wednesday:
--------

TD
DUBLIN -- A defiant Irish Prime Minister Brian Cowen is vowing to push through Europe's toughest
slash-and-tax budget in the face of voter fury, then defy the odds to win re-election despite a debt disaster
that has shaken the entire eurozone.
Cowen's vigorous defense of his embattled leadership comes a day after lawmakers narrowly backed a
2011 budget containing euro6 billion ($8 billion) in cuts and tax hikes that will take an estimated euro3,000
($4,000) per year out of average Irish households. The unprecedented scale of the budget-tightening was
a key condition for Ireland's recent agreement of a euro67.5 billion ($90 billion) EU-IMF rescue fund to
help Ireland cover its European-leading deficit and revive its debt-struck banks.

Wednesday's yields on 10-year bonds were little changed for the eurozone members rated most at risk of an eventual default, particularly Greece, which in May became the first eurozone member to be saved from bankruptcy. The most significant mover was Germany, whose benchmark bonds suffered a
moderate selloff, driving their 10-year yields above 3 percent for the first time since May's Greek crisis.

Traders said the selling reflected investors' increased appetite for higher-risk bonds versus the Germans' top-rated and consequently low-yielding debt securities.
------

LONDON -- European stocks traded in narrow ranges as bond market investors fretted about Europe's debt crisis and over the scale of U.S. borrowing following President Barack Obama's agreement with the Republicans to extend tax cuts.
In Europe, the FTSE 100 index of leading British shares closed down 13.92 points, or 0.2 percent, at
5,794.53 while Germany's DAX fell 26.04 points, or 0.4 percent, to 6,975.87. The CAC-40 in France
ended 21.48 points, or 0.6 percent, higher at 3,831.98.

More dramatic developments are being seen in the dollar and in U.S. government bonds following Obama's tax cuts compromise. Bond investors are worried there is no credible plan to get a grip on the U.S.'s own problems.

By late afternoon London time, the euro was trading 0.4 percent lower at $1.3226, while the dollar was 0.8 percent firmer at 84.22 yen.

Investors are also keeping a close watch on developments in China, amid mounting market talk that the country's monetary authorities are planning to raise interest rates soon to rein in inflationary pressures and cool a property-related credit boom.
The benchmark Shanghai Composite Index lost 1 percent to 2,848.55 while the Shenzhen Composite
Index for China's smaller, second market dropped 0.3 percent to 1,305.25. South Korea's Kospi slipped
0.4 percent to 1,955.72 and Hong Kong's Hang Seng lost 1.4 percent to 23,092.52.


Page 23 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
Japan's Nikkei 225 stock average bucked the trend, adding 91.23, or 0.9 percent, to 10,232.33 as the yen continued to weaken against the dollar to the relief of the country's exporters.
Oil prices slipped slightly to just above $88 a barrel after hitting a two-year high on Tuesday.
------

PRAGUE -- Thousands of angry state employees walk off the job across the Czech Republic to protest salary cuts, forcing the closure of hundreds of schools and government offices in what union leaders claimed was one of the largest protests in 20 years.

The strike, backed by the country's major umbrella union organization and the left-wing opposition, was aimed at a government plan to slash public sector pay by 10 percent as part of package of austerity measures. The union said that nearly 150,000 workers joined the protest in the country.

The government wants to eliminate the deficit by 2016, a plan that received positive reactions from rating agencies, but not from labor unions.
------

SKOPJE, Macedonia -- Macedonia has requested a credit line worth 480 million euros over two years from the International Monetary Fund -- seeking a safety net in the midst of Europe's debt crisis and bond-market turmoil.

IMF Managing Director Dominique Strauss-Kahn said he will "rapidly" seek approval of the request from the fund's executive board.

Macedonia's conservative government says it will use the money to support the budget and capital investments. It expects the economy to grow 2 percent this year and 3.5 percent in 2011. The former Yugoslav republic dipped in recession in 2009 with unemployment hovering around a staggering 30 percent.

The arrangement does not require economic austerity -- contrasting with the IMF's bailout loans to neighbor Greece, which is receiving euro110 billion from the fund and European countries after over-borrowing brought it to the brink of default.
------

BRUSSELS -- The EU competition watchdog fined five Taiwanese and South Korean electronics companies 649 million euros ($857 million) for fixing  prices on LCD panels between 2001 and 2006.

The companies include Chimei InnoLux Corp., LG Display Co., AU Optronics Corp., Chunghwa Picture Tubes Ltd. and HannStar Display Corp. Samsung Electronics Co., also participated in the price  fixing  but escaped a fine because it blew the whistle on the  cartel, the European Commission said.

Monday's fines targeted price-fixing  for LCD panels used in flat screens for televisions, computer monitors and electronic notebooks. The European Union's initial investigation had also included smaller LCD screens like the ones built into mobile phones, digital cameras, or MP3 players, but the  fines did not target price-fixing  for those products.

Between Oct. 2001 and Feb. 2006, the companies met about 60 times, mostly in Taiwanese hotels, for what they called "the Crystal meetings," the Commission said. In addition to  fixing  prices, they also exchanged information on their future production plans and other business plans, it said.
------

BERLIN -- Industrial production in Germany rose sharply in October and exports remained strong despite a month-on-month dip, indicating that Europe's biggest economy is still in good health amid troubles elsewhere on the continent.

Production was up 2.9 percent on the month, the Economy Ministry said -- led by a 4.6 percent increase in output of so-called investment goods such as machinery, a mainstay of the German economy. The increase followed a 1 percent dip in September, revised down from an initial reading of 0.8 percent.

Exports, meanwhile, declined by 1.1 percent on the month in October, giving up some of the previous month's sharp 3 percent gain, the Federal Statistical Office said. Germany, the world's second-biggest exporter after China, exported goods and services worth euro86.8 billion ($115.7 billion).
------

Page 24 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
LONDON -- Iceland's central bank has cut its key interest rate by 1 percentage point to 4.5 percent, continuing the bank's gradual lowering of the seven-day collateral lending rate as Iceland recovers from the global financial crisis.

The rate peaked at 18 percent in October 2008, when the country's banking system collapsed under the strain of the worldwide credit squeeze.
Sedlabanki also lowered its deposit and overnight lending rates.

HD       European regulator fines five LCD makers 648.9 million for price fixing
CR       Distributed by Contify.com
WC      412 words
PD       8 December 2010
SN      Domain-B SC      ATDOMB LA        English
CY       Copyright © 2010. The Information Company Pvt. Ltd.

LP
The European Union (EU) regulator today  fined five Taiwanese and a South Korean electronics companies a total of 648.9 million ($858 million), for  fixing  prices of liquid-crystal display (LCD) panels.

LCD panels are the main component of thin, flat screens used in televisions, computer monitors and electronic notebooks.

TD
Brussels-based EU's competition watchdog The  European Commission (EC) finedSamsung Electronics and LG Display of South Korea and AU Optronics, Chimei InnoLux Corp, Chunghwa Picture Tubes and HannStar Display Corp of Taiwan.

The EC gave Samsung full immunity from  fines under its leniency programme, as it was the first to provide information about the  cartel.

"Foreign companies, like European ones, need to understand that if they want to do business in Europe they must play fair. The companies concerned knew they were breaking competition rules and took steps to conceal their illegal behaviour.

The only understanding we will show is for those that come forward to denounce a  cartel and help prove its existence," said Joaquin Almunia, the vice president in charge of competition policy of EC.
The EC said that the six  LCD manufacturers operated as a  cartel between October 2001 and February
2006, during which, the companies agreed prices, including price ranges and minimum prices,
exchanged information on future production planning, capacity utilisation, pricing and other commercial
conditions.

The cartel members met more than 60 times mainly in hotels in Taiwan for what they called "the Crystal meetings," the EC said.

The EC said that these agreements had a direct impact on customers in the European Economic Area (EEA) because the vast majority of televisions, computer monitors and notebooks incorporating those LCD panels sold in the EEA came from Asia.

Chimei InnoLUx received the biggest  fine with 300 million, LG, the world's second-biggest  LCD maker has been fined 215 million, while AU Optronics $116.8 million, Chunghwa Picture Tubes 9 million and HannStar Display 8.1 million.

Following a December 2009 lawsuit by Nokia against eight LCD makers for forming a  cartel to fix price, (See: Nokia sues  LCD, CRT display makers for price-fixing
(http://www.domain-b.com/companies/companies_n/Nokia/20091202_price-fixing.html))  the US
regulator fined LG Display, Philips, Toshiba, Samsung, Chi Mei, Chunghwa, Sharp and Hitachi Displays
more than $890 million in criminal  fines.

BRUSSELS (Dow Jones)--The  European Commission Wednesday fined six makers of liquid crystal display screens a total of EUR649 million for operating a  cartel over five years.

Samsung Electronics (005930.SE) and LG Display (034220.SE) of Korea, and Taiwanese firms AU Optronics (2409.TW), Chimei InnoLux Corporation (3481.TW), Chunghwa Picture Tubes (2475.TW) and HannStar Display Corporation (6116.TW) agreed on prices and shared other commercial sensitive information at monthly meetings in hotels in Taiwan between 2001 and 2006.

HD          UPDATE: EU Fines 6 LCD Display Firms EUR649M For Fixing Prices
WC         277 words

(Adds comment from competition commissioner, context)



Carolyn Henson
Of DOW JONES NEWSWIRES

TD
BRUSSELS (Dow Jones)--The  European Commission Wednesday fined six makers of liquid crystal display screens a total of EUR649 million for operating a  cartel over five years.

Samsung Electronics (005930.SE) and LG Display (034220.SE) of Korea, and Taiwanese firms AU Optronics (2409.TW), Chimei InnoLux Corp. (3481.TW), Chunghwa Picture Tubes (2475.TW) and HannStar Display Corporation (6116.TW) met monthly in Taiwanese hotels to agree on prices and share other commercially sensitive information.

The companies knew their actions were illegal and took steps to conceal the locations and results of what they called "the Crystal meetings," which were around sixty in all, the commission said.

LG Display was fined EUR215 million, AU Optronics EUR117 million, Chimei InnoLux EUR300 million, Chungwa EUR9 million and HannStar EUR8 million. Samsung Electronics received full immunity from the fines for blowing the whistle on the  cartel.
"Foreign companies, like European ones, need to understand that if they want to do business in
Europe they must play fair," the EU's Competition Commissioner Joaquín Almunia said.

The price fixing  has a direct impact on European consumers as the display screens are used in televisions, computer monitors and laptops. Most of those products sold in the EU come from Asia, he added.
In setting the  fines, the commission took into account the level of sales the company has in the EU
and the duration of the  cartel.
-By Carolyn Henson, Dow Jones Newswires; +32 2 741 1 480; carolyn.henson@dowjones.com [

HD          2nd UPDATE: EU Fines Asian LCD Makers EUR649M For Fixing Prices
WC         426 words
PD          8 December 2010
ET          07:00 PM
SN          Dow Jones International News
SC          DJI
LA          English
CY          (c) 2010 Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP
(Adds detail)



By Carolyn Henson
Of DOW JONES NEWSWIRES

TD
BRUSSELS (Dow Jones)--The  European Commission Wednesday fined six Asian makers of liquid crystal display screens a total of EUR649 million for operating a price-fixing  cartel for almost five years.

Samsung Electronics (005930.SE) and LG Display (034220.SE) of Korea, and Taiwanese firms AU Optronics (2409.TW), Chimei InnoLux Corporation (3481.TW), Chunghwa Picture Tubes (2475.TW) and HannStar Display Corporation (6116.TW) met monthly in Taiwanese hotels to agree on prices and share other commercially sensitive information, the commission said.
The cartel ran from 2001 to 2006.

The commission fined LG Display EUR215 million, AU Optronics EUR117 million, Chimei InnoLux EUR300 million, Chungwa EUR9 million and HannStar EUR8 million. Samsung Electronics was granted immunity from the  fines for blowing the whistle on the  cartel.

The fines were based on European sales of more than EUR7 billion over the  cartel period, the commission said. The European Union has the power to  fine companies up to 10% of their global turnover for breaking its antitrust rules.

"Foreign companies, like European ones, have the obligation to respect competition rules when they do business in Europe," the EU's Competition chief Joaquin Almunia said. "The fact that the meetings took place outside of the EU is no excuse."

The companies knew their actions were illegal and took steps to conceal their gatherings, which they called "the Crystal meetings," the commissioner said. He added a  cartel document requested all the participants "to take care of confidentiality matters and to limit written communication."
There were around 60 meetings in all, Almunia said.

The cartel had a direct impact on European consumers as  LCD screens are used in televisions, computer monitors and laptops. Most of those products sold in the EU come from Asia, he added.

In setting the fines, the commission took into account the level of sales the company has in the EU and the duration of the cartel. It also reduced the  fines of some of the companies to reward their cooperation with the cartel investigation.
LG Display's price-fixing  penalty follows a $400 million  fine after a price-fixing  investigation in the
U.S. two years ago.
Chunghwa Picture Tubes had also pleaded guilty to price  fixing  in the same investigation.

No-one was immediately available at the companies to comment on the  fines.

HD               AU Optronics sales last month up by almost 5%; CARTEL FINES:Meanwhile,  AUO rivals such as Chi Mei Optoelectronics and LG Display could be fined up to 700 million euros for fixing  prices of LCD panels
BY                By Kevin Chen
CR               Staff Reporter, with Bloomberg
WC               628 words
PD                8 December 2010
SN                Taipei Times
SC                TAIP
LA                English
CY                © Copyright 2010 The Taipei Times. All rights reserved.

LP
With panel shipments increasing across the board last month, AU Optronics Corp (AUO, ) yesterday said that preliminary consolidated revenue last month reached NT$36.87 billion (US$1.2 billion), up 4.95 percent from October, but down 4.03 percent from a year earlier because falling prices, a company statement showed.

The Hsinchu-based company posted consolidated revenues of NT$35.13 billion in October, the lowest since Februarys NT$32.67 billion, and NT$38.42 billion in November last year.

TD
The company, the nations No. 2 flat-panel maker by revenue after Chimei Innolux Corp, said that shipments of large-sized panels last month rose 6.3 percent from the previous month to about 9.72
-million units, while those of small and medium-sized panels edged up 1.5 percent to 18.04 million units.

Large-sized panels refer to models that are 10 inches or more and that are mainly used in desktop monitors, notebook computers and  LCD TVs, while small to medium-sized panels refer to those under 10 inches that are used in smartphones and netbooks.

Consolidated revenue in the first 11 months of the year totaled NT$436.55 billion, up 35.37 percent from NT$322.5 billion in the same period last year, the firm said.

On Oct. 27, the company said that shipments of large-sized panels would likely grow by 3 to 5 percent quarter-on-quarter from the 28.7 million units shipped in the third quarter, but that the average selling price would likely fall further this quarter.

Prices of flat panels have been undergoing a prolonged downward spiral in recent months due to excessive inventories. In the first half of this month, IT panel prices remained flat from the last two weeks of last month, while TV panel prices continued to display a slower decline, market researcher DisplaySearchs data showed.

Citigroup analyst Jonathan Rhee said he expected IT panel prices to rebound in the fourth quarter, while TV panel prices will drop at a slower rate.

We expect IT panel customers to start restocking given limited room for further price drops. However, we expect TV panel prices to continue to decline albeit more mildly, given
less-than-strong Chinese demand after the Chinese Golden Week and still relatively weak North
American demand, he said in a report on Sunday.
EU FINES

Meanwhile, LG Display Co, Chi Mei Optoelectronics Corp and three other companies may be  fined up to 700 million euros (US$930 million) by the EU for  fixing  the price of  LCD panels, Reuters reported.


Page 34 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
Samsung Electronics Co may escape  fines, to be levied today, because it was the first in the  cartel
to inform the  European Commission, Reuters said on Monday.

LCD panels are used in mobile phones, televisions and computers.

Chi Mei, which merged with Innolux Display Corp in March to form Chimei Innolux Corp, pleaded guilty to US antitrust charges last year and agreed to pay US$220 million in  fines.

LG Display and Samsung Electronics said in 2006 they were being probed by regulators around the world over alleged price fixing.
AU Optronics said it received a formal complaint from the  European Commission in May last year. Lee Bang-soo, a spokesman for LG Display, didnt immediately respond to a call or e-mail outside
normal office hours. Likewise, a call to Samsung Electronics in Seoul and calls and e-mails to Chi
Mei representatives Eddie Chen and Loreta Chen went unanswered outside business hours.

HD           EU Fines LCD Firms for Price Fixing
BY           By Carolyn Henson

BRUSSELS—The  European Commission on Wednesday fined six makers of liquid-crystal display screens a total of €649 million ($861 million) for allegedly operating a  cartel over five years.

The commission, the European Union's executive arm, said Samsung Electronics Co. and LG Display Co. of South Korea and Taiwanese producers AU Optronics Corp., Chimei InnoLux Corp., Chunghwa Picture Tubes and HannStar Display Corp. met monthly in Taiwanese hotels from 2001 to 2006 to agree on prices and share commercially sensitive information.

TD
The commission said LG Display was  fined €215 million, AU Optronics €117 million, Chimei InnoLux
€300 million, Chungwa €9 million and HannStar €8 million. Samsung Electronics got full immunity from
the fines for blowing the whistle on the  cartel.

The fines took into account each company's share of the more than €7 billion in  LCD sales in Europe over the cartel period, the commission said. But it reduced the  fines of some of the companies to reward their cooperation with the  cartel investigation. The EU has the power to  fine companies as much as 10% of their global revenue for breaking its antitrust rules.

The EU's action comes two years after LG Display paid a $400 million  fine and pleaded guilty to criminal price-fixing  charges in the U.S. Chunghwa Picture Tubes pleaded guilty in the same U.S. investigation.
Representatives of the companies weren't available to comment Wednesday .

The LCD makers fined by the EU knew their actions were illegal and took steps to conceal their gatherings, which they called "the crystal meetings," said EU Competition Commissioner Joaquín Almunia. There were around 60 such meetings in all, the commissioner said.

He added that a  cartel document asked all the participants "to take care of confidentiality matters and to limit written communication."

"Foreign companies, like European ones, have the obligation to respect competition rules when they do business in Europe," Mr. Almunia said.

LCD screens are used in televisions, computer monitors and laptops.

HD       Taiwan panel maker to appeal EU price-fixing fine
WC      369 words
PD       8 December 2010
SN       Central News Agency English News
SC       CNAENG
LA        English
CY       (c) 2010 All materials contained on this site may not be reproduced, distributed, transmitted, displayed, published or broadcast without the prior written permission of the Central News Agency.

LP
Taipei, Dec. 8 (CNA) AU Optronics Corp. of Taiwan said Wednesday night that it will appeal a  European
Commission decision to slap heavy fines on it and three other Taiwanese flat panel makers and a
South Korean manufacturer for allegedly fixing  prices on the EU market.

AUO, Chi Mei Optoelectronics Corp., Chunghwa Picture Tubes Ltd. and HannStar Display Corp. were fined a total of 433.92 million euro (some NT$17.3 billion) for violating EU's competition rules and trying to hide their "law-breaking behavior."

TD
An AUO spokesman said it has cooperated with EU authorities over the past four years in their investigation into industry practices regarding the production and marketing of TFT-LCD products.

The company, which was  fined 116.8 million euro, has decided to file an appeal with the General Court in Luxemburg and vigorously defend its business practices, the spokesman said.

Chi Mei and Chunghwa said they are taking a closer look at the EU decision before taking their next steps. A Chi Mei executive said the  fine on his company, 300 million euro, is "really too harsh." Chunghua was fined 9.02 million euro.
HannStar Display Corp., which got a  fine of 8.1 million euro, would not comment on the EC action. Market analysts said the Taiwanese manufacturers are not making big profits and the  fines are "simply
too heavy."

The Ministry of Economic Affairs (MOEA) said the government would provide all necessary assistance to the manufacturers.

Duh Tyzz-jiun, director general of the MOEA's Industrial Development Bureau, told the Central News Agency that as long as the accused companies need assistance when facing disciplinary action, the government would try its best to help them.

Duh and other economics officials admitted the heavy  fines will have impacts on Taiwan's flat panel industry.
LG Display of South Korea was also on the hitting list, being given a 215 million euro  fine. Samsung Electronics of South Korea, the world's largest flat panel maker, was not charged since it
alerted the  European Commission to the price-fixing  practices.
(By Tsao Yu-fan, Lin Shu-yuanm Pan CHih-yi and S.C. Chang)

BRUSSELS/PRAGUE (CIA) - The European Commission has fined six LCD panel producers a total of EUR 649 mln for operating a cartel which harmed European buyers of television sets, computers and other products that use the key Liquid Crystal Display component, Commission Vice President in charge of competition policy Joaquin Almunia said in a press conference on Wednesday, December 8.

The cartel agreement was reported by South Korean Samsung Electronics, which thus avoided the  fine. It will be the eighth highest  fine from the fines imposed by the European Commission on groups of firms due to the violation of business competition rules.

HD        Display panel cartel fined €649m
BY         By Nikki Tait in Brussels
WC        423 words
PD         8 December 2010
SN         Financial Times (FT.Com)
SC         FTCOM
LA         English
CY         Copyright 2010 The Financial Times Ltd. All rights reserved. Please do not cut and paste FT articles and redistribute by email or post to the web.

LP
Five Taiwanese and South Korean electronics companies in a  cartel with Samsung have been  fined a total of €648.9m ($858m) by Europe's antitrust watchdog. The companies ran their operation in the market for display panels that are used in consumer gadgets.

The five companies are LG Display of South Korea and Taiwan's AU Optronics, Chimei Innolux, Chunghwa Picture Tubes and HannStar Display.

TD
Samsung blew the whistle on the  cartel and so escaped penalty.

EU officials said on Wednesday that the companies met more than 60 times over about four years to agree prices, production schedules and other commercial conditions.

The assignations, called "the crystal meetings", took place mainly in Taiwanese hotels, but had a big knock-on effect in Europe, where large volumes of televisions, computer monitors and notebooks using the panels were sold.

The biggest single penalty will be paid by Chimei, at €300m. LG Display faces a €215m  fine, but this came after significant reductions because the company co-operated and was the first to produce evidence that the  cartel continued beyond 2005. It received partial immunity.

Of the other three companies, AU Optronics is  fined €116.8m, after getting a 20 per cent reduction for co-operation; Chunghwa pays €9.025m after a 5 per cent reduction for co-operation; and HannStar is fined €8.1m.

Joaquín Almunia, EU competition commissioner, said the case showed that "foreign companies, like European ones, need to understand that if they want to do business in Europe they must play fair". "The companies concerned knew that they were breaking competition rules and took steps to conceal their illegal behaviour."

He added that two of the companies, who remain unidentified, had asked for reductions in  fines on grounds of financial hardship and "inability to pay," but that these arguments did not succeed.
In similar probes into the  LCD market in the US and Japan, Japanese companies were also penalised. Mr Almunia said that there had been no proof that their products were involved in the particular markets
that were examined by the  European Commission, which included thin-film  LCD panels used in
computers, mobile phones, TVs, digital watches, pocket calculators and MP3 players.

This is the seventh  cartel case dealt with by Brussels this year, and takes the total amount of  fines to in excess of €3bn. The record annual total was in 2007 when  fines topped €3.3bn on aggregate. Between
2006 and 2010 fines have exceeded €1.5bn a year.

HD            UPDATE 1-EU fines LG Display, Chi Mei, others 649 mln euros
WC           428 words

LP
* Chi Mei has biggest  fine of 300 mln euros
* AU Optronics Corp, Chunghwa Picture Tubes also penalised

TD
* Fine for HannStar
* No fine for Samsung Electronics, alerted  EU Commission
* U.S. probe of sector led to criminal  fines above $890 mln
(Adds fines, Commissioner comments) By Foo Yun Chee
BRUSSELS, Dec 8 (Reuters) - LG Display, Chi Mei Optoelectronics Corp and three other firms were fined a total of 649 million euros ($858 million) by EU regulators on Wednesday for  fixing  prices of display panels used in consumer devices.

The European Commission, the EU antitrust watchdog, charged the companies in July last year with breaching EU laws on restrictive business practices, while other regulators around the world have
also investigated the sector.

Chi Mei, now part of Chi Mei Innolux, Taiwan's largest maker of  LCD panels, was hit with the biggest fine of 300 million euros. It paid $220 million in  fines last year after pleading guilty to U.S. charges of price fixing.

LG Display, the world's second-biggest  LCD maker, and AU Optronics were penalised 215 million euros and 116.8 million euros respectively.

A fine of 9 million euros was levied on Taiwanese firm Chunghwa Picture Tubes and of 8.1 million euros on HannStar Display Corp.World No.1  LCD maker Samsung Electronics was not  fined as it alerted the Commission to the  cartel.
"Foreign companies, like European ones, need to understand that if they want to do business in
Europe they must play fair," EU Competition Commissioner Joaquin Almunia said in a statement.
The Commission, which can penalise companies up to 10 percent of their global turnover for
infringing EU laws, said the  cartel operated between October 2001 and February 2006 and met about
60 times in "crystal meetings".
Almunia said the investigation did not find any proof that Japanese  LCD makers were involved. In the U.S. Department of Justice investigation, eight companies, including LG Display, Chi Mei,
Chunghwa, Japanese company Sharp Corp and Hitachi Displays, paid more than $890 million in
criminal fines for price fixing.

Japan's Fair Trade Commission slapped  fines on Sharp Corp and Hitachi Ltd in 2008 for price  fixing
in the market for  LCD panels.
Page 45 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
The EU Commission's case had centred on thin-film liquid crystal display panels used in computers, mobile phones, televisions, digital watches, pocket calculators and MP3 players.

SEOUL, Dec 9 (Reuters) - South Korea's LG Display said on Thursday it may appeal a decision by the European Commission to impose a 215 million euro ($285 million)  fine for a violation of the competition law.

On Wednesday LG and four other display firms were  fined a total of 649 million euros by EU regulators for  fixing  prices of display panels used in consumer devices such as TVs, computers and notebooks. [ID:nLDE6B6276]

TD
"LG Display acknowledges the wrongful acts of the past and respects the  European Commission's regulatory authority in this regard," the world's No.2  LCD flat screen maker said in a statement.

"However, LG Display may, after careful review and consideration, appeal today's decision to the EU General Court if it finds there were procedural or substantive due process issues with the investigation."

HD      EU slaps 860-million-dollar fine on LCD makers for price fixing

SC      TRENDE

CY      (c) 2010 Trend News Agency. Copyright for the present information is reserved, in case of reprint of any part of it reference should be done to the Agency.

LP
The European Commission on Wednesday imposed a 649-million-euro (860-million-dollar) antitrust  fine on a cartel of manufacturers of liquid crystal display (LCD) screens for computers and televisions, DPA reports. EU competition commissioner Joaquin Almunia said Samsung and LG of Korea, AU Optronics, Chimei InnoLux, Chungwa Picture Tubes and HannStar Display Corporation were found to have colluded from 2001 to 2006 to fix prices and exchange industrial information. Samsung was rewarded for blowing the whistle on the illegal arrangement with a total exemption from  fines, while LG was hit with a
215-million-euro bill. Chimei was ordered to pay 300 million euros, AU Optronics 116.8, Chunghwa 9 and HannStar 8.1, Almunia said. Two companies - unnamed to protect their commercial interests - asked for a discount claiming they were in financial dire straits, but EU officials "concluded that neither request was justified," Almunia said.

TD
The commissioner stressed that non-EU companies are subject to EU antitrust rules if they sell their products in the bloc, even if their cartel meetings take place outside of the EU's jurisdiction. Wednesday's decision was the seventh cartel fine the EU executive imposed in 2010, bringing the year's total to over 3 billion euros. EU rules prohibit price-fixing  and other market manipulation. The EU's executive arm, has a long record of breaking up cartels, issuing  fines worth billions of dollars in the process.

(Gold is the February contract on the Comex division of the New York Mercantile Exchange, silver and copper are the March contracts, and oil is January.)

NEW YORK - The compromise backed by President Barack Obama and Republican leaders on extending tax cuts crushed bonds on Wednesday as traders expected the plan to lead to higher budget deficits and a pickup in economic growth. Stocks swung between modest gains and losses.

Treasury prices dropped sharply, sending their yields higher for a second day. The yield on the 10-year Treasury note rose to 3.28 per cent, the highest level since June 15 and a huge jump from the 2.93 per cent it was trading at on Monday before the tax deal was announced.




Page 50 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
Economists are raising their estimates for economic growth as a result of the tax-cut package. Goldman Sachs economists released a rough estimate Wednesday saying that the tax relief could wind up adding between 0.5 and one percentage point to economic growth next year.
Stock indices opened higher but turned mixed in early afternoon trading.
The Dow Jones industrial average was 6.7 points higher, by 0.06 per cent, to 11,365.86. The broader
Standard & Poor's 500 index rose 2.98 or 0.24 per cent, to 1,226.63. The Nasdaq composite index rose
7.98, or 0.31 per cent, to 2,606.47.
The higher rates in the Treasury market helped push the dollar up against other currencies including the
Japanese yen and the euro. The dollar rose 0.4 per cent against an index of six other major currencies.

LONDON - The European single currency dipped against the dollar on Wednesday, with the greenback still benefiting from the prospect of extended US tax cuts and stubborn worries over the eurozone debt crisis.
The euro weakened to 1.3226 dollars in late afternoon trading in London, from 1.3258 dollars late on
Tuesday in New York.
The dollar meanwhile gained against the Japanese unit, trading at 84.20 yen against 83.45 yen on
Tuesday.

European stocks were mixed, with the London FTSE 100 index of leading shares dropping 0.24 per cent at 5,794.53 points.

In Paris, the CAC 40 climbed 0.56 per cent to 3,831.98 points while in Frankfurt the DAX per cent slipped 0.37 per cent to 6,975.87 points.

Elsewhere, Madrid gained 1.55 per cent, Milan 1.40 per cent, Lisbon 0.89 per cent, Swiss shares 0.71 per cent, and Amsterdam 0.15 per cent. Brussels dropped 0.28 per cent.

TOKYO - Japan's Nikkei average closed up 0.9 per cent on Wednesday after briefly hitting its highest level in almost seven months, as the dollar's rise against the yen encouraged buying after Tokyo stocks had fallen during the previous two sessions.

Foreign fund operators were keen on investing in lagging Tokyo equities but the Nikkei's advance was limited ahead of the settlement of futures and options prices on Friday, analysts said.

The Nikkei gained 91.23 points to 10,232.33, having touched an intraday high of 10,258.90, its highest level since May 18.
The broader Topix index rose 0.9 per cent to 887.39.

HONG KONG - Hong Kong shares fell 1.43 per cent and Shanghai lost 0.95 per cent on Wednesday as traders awaited a possible interest rate rise on the mainland aimed at damping down inflation.

Expectations of a rate rise have grown ahead of key economic data for November, which the mainland authorities said would be released this coming Saturday instead of the following Monday as scheduled earlier.
In Hong Kong, the benchmark Hang Seng Index shed 335.63 points to end at 23,092.52. Turnover was
$HK77.71 billion ($A10.18 billion).
In Shanghai, the Composite Index, which covers both A and B shares, was down 27.31 points at
2,848.55 on turnover of 110.2 billion yuan ($A16.7 billion).
Gold miners led the decline as the price of the precious metal slipped from a record high on Tuesday. Asian stock markets mostly fell amid expectations of the possible Chinese interest rate rise.
In other markets, Seoul closed 0.35 per cent lower, Taipei was flat, Jakarta rose 1.28 per cent, Singapore rose 0.34 per cent, Kuala Lumpur rose 0.55 per cent, Bangkok fell 1.50 per cent, or 15.64 points, and Mumbai fell 1.19 per cent.

WELLINGTON - The New Zealand sharemarket posted modest gains as other markets faltered while investors waited for the Reserve Bank of New Zealand's (RBNZ's) latest assessment of the economy on Thursday.


Page 51 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
The benchmark NZX-50 index closed up 12.478 points, or 0.38 per cent, at 3,294.336, after closing on
Wednesday down 11.3 points.

Stuart Hardie at Craigs Investment Partners said strength in selective leaders pushed the index higher on a day there was little corporate news to trade on.

SYDNEY - The Australian market is receiving mixed leads from offshore trading overnight, with securities indices mixed, whilst precious metals and oil were lower. The US dollar rose.
On the ASX 24 at 0704 AEDT, the December share price index futures contract was 16 points higher at
4,716.

In economics news on Thursday, the Australian Bureau of Statistics releases labour force data for November, and the Australian Office of Financial Management conducts a tender process to issue $600 million of Treasury Notes maturing on February 11, 2011, and $600 million of Treasury Notes maturing on April 29, 2011.
In equities news, Ten Network Holdings Ltd and Bank Of Queensland Ltd hold annual general meetings. Westfield Group holds a security holder meeting to approve the proposal to establish the Westfield Retail
Trust.

On Wednesday, financial stocks dragged the Australian share market lower from an almost one month high after the Federal Treasurer pledged to release banking competition measures within the next week.

The benchmark S&P/ASX200 index declined 26.9 points, or 0.57 per cent, to close at 4,699.9 on Wednesday, while the broader All Ordinaries index fell 24.3 points, or 0.5 per cent, to 4,791.7. The All Ords closed at 4,816 on Tuesday, the highest since November 10.
ENERGY
World oil prices fell toward $US88 on Wednesday as many traders took profits and digested a mixed US
energy report, after the market had struck recent two-year peaks, analysts said.

In mid-afternoon trade, New York's main contract, light sweet crude for January, had retreated 27 cents at $US88.42 a barrel, one day after hitting 90.76, a level last seen on October 8, 2008.

Prior to Wednesday, the oil market was boosted by a cold snap in Europe and rising sentiment over the global economic outlook, but eurozone debt crisis worries were also weighing on crude markets, traders said.

Elsewhere, the US government's Department of Energy (DoE) announced on Wednesday that American crude oil reserves sank by 3.8 million barrels in the week ending December 3.

That compared with market expectations for a lighter drop of 1.2 million barrels, according to analysts polled by Dow Jones Newswires.

The DoE added, however, that gasoline or petrol stockpiles advanced by 3.8 million barrels last week. Market expectations had been for a small gain of 100,000 barrels.
PRECIOUS METALS

Gold prices fell more than one per cent for a second day on Wednesday as an extended fall in US Treasury prices fuelled profit-taking from bullion's record run by investors seeking better yield returns.

Spot gold traded at $1,381.35 an ounce, down 1.4 per cent, at 12:39 pm EST (1739 GMT), having earlier fallen by as much as 2.1 per cent to a one-week low of $1,371.45. US gold futures for February delivery fell $26 to $1,383 an ounce.

Technical selling accelerated the decline in silver prices, which had jumped to a 30-year high above $30 an ounce, but investment interest remained high as the world's largest silver-backed exchange-traded fund hit another record high.

Silver dropped one per cent to $28.37 an ounce, causing the gold/silver ratio to stabilise hear a near-four year low.

Gold has lost some safe-haven appeal as, for the first time in weeks, euro zone debt concerns were placed on the back burner and investors focused on US economic fundamentals in a thinning market.


Page 52 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
Gold hit an all-time high at $1,430.95 an ounce on Tuesday, but has now fallen by about 4 per cent after the rally ran out of steam.

The world's largest silver ETF, iShares Silver Trust, said its holdings hit another record at 10,941.34 tonnes by Wednesday.
Setting gold on the back foot early in the day was a rally in the dollar, after the proposed extension in US
tax cuts prompted a spike in bond yields on Tuesday, which in turn raised the cost of holding gold to
non-US investors.
Platinum dropped 0.9 per cent to $1,674 an ounce, while palladium slipped 0.5 per cent to $726.47. BASE METALS
Copper ended sharply higher on Wednesday, moving back up against record highs, as supply-side constraints continued to draw in strong investment demand flows, even as the dollar rose and rate hike concerns in top-consumer China mounted.

Copper's bullish momentum picked up late in the day, while surrounding markets like gold, silver and crude oil slipped, reinforcing the red metal's strong fundamental backdrop.

On the London Metal Exchange (LME), three-month copper closed up $245 at $9,015 a tonne, well within striking distance of Tuesday's record high of $9,044.

COMEX copper for March delivery climbed 5.10 cents, or nearly 1.3 per cent, to finish at $4.1005 per lb, near its own record at $4.1315 per lb.

Stocks of copper at LME warehouses have declined since February, indicating a pick-up in demand and against a backdrop of tight supply.

The latest data showed stocks fell 1,125 tonnes to 350,250 tonnes, on their way to the biggest annual decline in six years.

The prospects of an undersupplied market have helped boost the price of metal for nearby delivery to a premium against the benchmark contract since early November.
Among other metals, aluminum ended up $70 at $2,375 a tonne.
Some term premiums for primary aluminum shipments to Japan for January-March were agreed at
$112-$113 per tonne, a trader said, marking the lowest level in six quarters and the fourth straight
quarterly drop.
Tin was untraded at the close but last bid at $25,600 a tonne.

Top tin producer Indonesia forecast tin output will climb to 95,097 tonnes in 2011, from 54,646 tonnes this year.

WELLINGTON - The New Zealand Reserve Bank has left the official cash rate unchanged at three per cent, as expected, it was announced.

NEW YORK - US stocks closed modestly higher on Wednesday as traders awaited developments on a controversial tax-cuts deal that is seen key to the economic recovery.

In a day lacking major market movers and economic indicators, the spotlight turned to the spectacular debut of two Chinese internet companies on Wall Street.
The Dow Jones Industrial Average had advanced 13.32 points (0.12 per cent) to 11,372.48 when
markets settled, while the S&P 500 index, a broader measure of the market, gained 4.53 points (0.37 per
cent) to 1,228.28.


Page 56 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
The tech-rich Nasdaq climbed 10.67 points (0.41 per cent) to 2,609.16.

The compromise between President Barack Obama and his Republican foes would see an extension of tax breaks to all income classes, including the wealthiest Americans, which Obama had vehemently opposed.

The deal was seen by many economists as key to the US economic recovery, with Goldman Sachs analysts estimating the package could roughly add 0.5 to 1.0 percentage point to gross domestic product growth in 2011.

The biggest winners of the day were two Chinese companies that made stellar initial public offerings (IPOs) on Wednesday, highlighting traders' thirst for stakes in firms based in the world's fastest growing economy.

Dangdang, China's largest online book retailer, boasting an impressive 50 per cent hold of the market, saw its shares trade at $US29.91, 87 per cent higher than their initial price tag.
And Youku.com, the Chinese equivalent of the hugely popular Youtube online video website, fetched
33.44 dollars, a whopping 161 per cent above its offering price.

LONDON - The European single currency dipped against the dollar on Wednesday, with the greenback still benefiting from the prospect of extended US tax cuts and stubborn worries over the eurozone debt crisis.
The euro weakened to 1.3226 dollars in late afternoon trading in London, from 1.3258 dollars late on
Tuesday in New York.
The dollar meanwhile gained against the Japanese unit, trading at 84.20 yen against 83.45 yen on
Tuesday.

European stocks were mixed, with the London FTSE 100 index of leading shares dropping 0.24 per cent at 5,794.53 points.

Elsewhere, Madrid gained 1.55 per cent, Milan 1.40 per cent, Lisbon 0.89 per cent, Swiss shares 0.71 per cent, and Amsterdam 0.15 per cent. Brussels dropped 0.28 per cent.

HONG KONG - Hong Kong shares fell 1.43 per cent and Shanghai lost 0.95 per cent on Wednesday as traders awaited a possible interest rate rise on the mainland aimed at damping down inflation.

Gold miners led the decline as the price of the precious metal slipped from a record high on Tuesday. Asian stock markets mostly fell amid expectations of the possible Chinese interest rate rise.



Page 57 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
In other markets, Seoul closed 0.35 per cent lower, Taipei was flat, Jakarta rose 1.28 per cent, Singapore rose 0.34 per cent, Kuala Lumpur rose 0.55 per cent, Bangkok fell 1.50 per cent, or 15.64 points, and Mumbai fell 1.19 per cent.

WELLINGTON - The New Zealand sharemarket posted modest gains as other markets faltered while investors waited for the Reserve Bank of New Zealand's (RBNZ's) latest assessment of the economy on Thursday.
The benchmark NZX-50 index closed up 12.478 points, or 0.38 per cent, at 3,294.336, after closing on
Wednesday down 11.3 points.

Stuart Hardie at Craigs Investment Partners said strength in selective leaders pushed the index higher on a day there was little corporate news to trade on.

SYDNEY - The Australian market is receiving mixed leads from offshore trading overnight, with securities indices mixed, whilst precious metals and oil were lower. The US dollar rose.
On the ASX 24 at 0824 AEDT, the December share price index futures contract was 19 points higher at
4,719.

In economics news on Thursday, the Australian Bureau of Statistics releases labour force data for November, and the Australian Office of Financial Management conducts a tender process to issue $600 million of Treasury Notes maturing on February 11, 2011, and $600 million of Treasury Notes maturing on April 29, 2011.
In equities news, Ten Network Holdings Ltd and Bank Of Queensland Ltd hold annual general meetings. Westfield Group holds a security holder meeting to approve the proposal to establish the Westfield Retail
Trust.

On Wednesday, financial stocks dragged the Australian share market lower from an almost one month high after the Federal Treasurer pledged to release banking competition measures within the next week.

The benchmark S&P/ASX200 index declined 26.9 points, or 0.57 per cent, to close at 4,699.9 on Wednesday, while the broader All Ordinaries index fell 24.3 points, or 0.5 per cent, to 4,791.7. The All Ords closed at 4,816 on Tuesday, the highest since November 10.
ENERGY

Oil prices fell toward $US88 a barrel as many traders took profits and digested a mixed US energy reserves report, after the market had struck recent two-year peaks.

New York's main contract, light sweet crude for January, retreated 41 cents to settle at $US88.28 a barrel, a day after hitting $US90.76, a level last seen on October 8, 2008.

And in London, Brent North Sea crude for delivery in January shed 62 cents to close at $US90.77 per barrel, after hitting a 26-month high at $US92.86 on Tuesday.

Prior to Wednesday, the oil market was boosted by a cold snap in Europe and rising optimism about the global economic outlook.

However, worries about the eurozone sovereign debt crisis were also weighing on crude oil markets, traders said.

The US government's Department of Energy (DoE) reported Wednesday that American crude oil reserves sank by 3.8 million barrels in the week ending December 3.

That compared with market expectations for a much smaller drop of 1.2 million barrels, according to analysts polled by Dow Jones Newswires.

The DoE added that gasoline stockpiles advanced by 3.8 million barrels last week, however, sharply higher than the expected gain of 100,000 barrels.
PRECIOUS METALS

Gold prices fell more than one per cent for a second day on Wednesday as an extended fall in US Treasury prices fuelled profit-taking from bullion's record run by investors seeking better yield returns.



Page 58 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
Spot gold traded at $1,381.35 an ounce, down 1.4 per cent, at 12:39 pm EST (1739 GMT), having earlier fallen by as much as 2.1 per cent to a one-week low of $1,371.45. US gold futures for February delivery fell $26 to $1,383 an ounce.

Technical selling accelerated the decline in silver prices, which had jumped to a 30-year high above $30 an ounce, but investment interest remained high as the world's largest silver-backed exchange-traded fund hit another record high.

Silver dropped one per cent to $28.37 an ounce, causing the gold/silver ratio to stabilise hear a near-four year low.

Gold has lost some safe-haven appeal as, for the first time in weeks, euro zone debt concerns were placed on the back burner and investors focused on US economic fundamentals in a thinning market.

Gold hit an all-time high at $1,430.95 an ounce on Tuesday, but has now fallen by about 4 per cent after the rally ran out of steam.

The world's largest silver ETF, iShares Silver Trust, said its holdings hit another record at 10,941.34 tonnes by Wednesday.
Setting gold on the back foot early in the day was a rally in the dollar, after the proposed extension in US
tax cuts prompted a spike in bond yields on Tuesday, which in turn raised the cost of holding gold to
non-US investors.
Platinum dropped 0.9 per cent to $1,674 an ounce, while palladium slipped 0.5 per cent to $726.47. BASE METALS
Copper ended sharply higher on Wednesday, moving back up against record highs, as supply-side constraints continued to draw in strong investment demand flows, even as the dollar rose and rate hike concerns in top-consumer China mounted.

Copper's bullish momentum picked up late in the day, while surrounding markets like gold, silver and crude oil slipped, reinforcing the red metal's strong fundamental backdrop.

On the London Metal Exchange (LME), three-month copper closed up $245 at $9,015 a tonne, well within striking distance of Tuesday's record high of $9,044.

COMEX copper for March delivery climbed 5.10 cents, or nearly 1.3 per cent, to finish at $4.1005 per lb, near its own record at $4.1315 per lb.

Stocks of copper at LME warehouses have declined since February, indicating a pick-up in demand and against a backdrop of tight supply.

The latest data showed stocks fell 1,125 tonnes to 350,250 tonnes, on their way to the biggest annual decline in six years.

The prospects of an undersupplied market have helped boost the price of metal for nearby delivery to a premium against the benchmark contract since early November.
Among other metals, aluminum ended up $70 at $2,375 a tonne.
Some term premiums for primary aluminum shipments to Japan for January-March were agreed at
$112-$113 per tonne, a trader said, marking the lowest level in six quarters and the fourth straight
quarterly drop.
Tin was untraded at the close but last bid at $25,600 a tonne.

Top tin producer Indonesia forecast tin output will climb to 95,097 tonnes in 2011, from 54,646 tonnes this year.
INTERNATIONAL NEWS

DUBLIN - Prime Minister Brian Cowen said the Irish became drunk with success during economic boom years, as he defended painful austerity measures being imposed as part of an international bailout of the debt-laden nation.

GENEVA - The head of the IMF Dominique Strauss-Kahn said the situation in Europe, which is battling a debt crisis, remains troubling and that the future looked uncertain.

Page 59 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
BRUSSELS - The  European Commission imposed 649 million euros ($A876.08 million) in  fines on South Korean and Taiwanese electronics firms for secret backroom price-fixing  of LCD flat screens for Europe's TVs and computers.

BERLIN - Industrial production in Germany rose sharply in October and exports remained strong despite a month-on-month dip, indicating that Europe's biggest economy is still in good health amid troubles elsewhere on the continent.

WASHINGTON - The International Monetary Fund welcomed the Irish parliament's approval of the first technical measures of the 2011 budget aimed at rescuing the country from a deficit crisis.

WASHINGTON - Electronic payments have surged in the United States to more than 75 per cent of all noncash payments as check usage continues to fall by the wayside, a Federal Reserve report showed.

LONDON - The European single currency dipped against the dollar, with the greenback still benefiting from the prospect of extended US tax cuts and stubborn worries over the eurozone debt crisis.

LONDON - Anglo-Australian miner Rio Tinto and Canada's Ivanhoe Mines said they had reached agreement on the joint development of the Oyu Tolgoi copper and gold project in Mongolia.

WELLINGTON - The Reserve Bank of New Zealand left the official cash rate (OCR) unchanged at three per cent as growth continues to moderate, but rebuilding following $5 billion worth of earthquake damage in Canterbury is expected to help boost the economy.

WELLINGTON - New Zealand wineries are on a slippery slope, facing steadily declining profitability and rising debt, with prospects for improvement unlikely in the short term, a new survey says.

WELLINGTON - The New Zealand Reserve Bank has left the official cash rate unchanged at three per cent, as expected, it was announced.
