(Gold is the February contract on the Comex division of the New York Mercantile Exchange, silver and copper are the March contracts, and oil is January.)

NEW YORK - US stocks closed modestly higher on Wednesday as traders awaited developments on a controversial tax-cuts deal that is seen key to the economic recovery.

In a day lacking major market movers and economic indicators, the spotlight turned to the spectacular debut of two Chinese internet companies on Wall Street.




Page 63 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
The Dow Jones Industrial Average had advanced 13.32 points (0.12 per cent) to 11,372.48 when
markets settled, while the S&P 500 index, a broader measure of the market, gained 4.53 points (0.37 per
cent) to 1,228.28.
The tech-rich Nasdaq climbed 10.67 points (0.41 per cent) to 2,609.16.

The compromise between President Barack Obama and his Republican foes would see an extension of tax breaks to all income classes, including the wealthiest Americans, which Obama had vehemently opposed.

The deal was seen by many economists as key to the US economic recovery, with Goldman Sachs analysts estimating the package could roughly add 0.5 to 1.0 percentage point to gross domestic product growth in 2011.

The biggest winners of the day were two Chinese companies that made stellar initial public offerings (IPOs) on Wednesday, highlighting traders' thirst for stakes in firms based in the world's fastest growing economy.

Dangdang, China's largest online book retailer, boasting an impressive 50 per cent hold of the market, saw its shares trade at $US29.91, 87 per cent higher than their initial price tag.
And Youku.com, the Chinese equivalent of the hugely popular Youtube online video website, fetched
33.44 dollars, a whopping 161 per cent above its offering price.

LONDON - The European single currency dipped against the dollar on Wednesday, with the greenback still benefiting from the prospect of extended US tax cuts and stubborn worries over the eurozone debt crisis.
The euro weakened to 1.3226 dollars in late afternoon trading in London, from 1.3258 dollars late on
Tuesday in New York.
The dollar meanwhile gained against the Japanese unit, trading at 84.20 yen against 83.45 yen on
Tuesday.

European stocks were mixed, with the London FTSE 100 index of leading shares dropping 0.24 per cent at 5,794.53 points.
In Paris, the CAC 40 climbed 0.56 per cent to 3,831.98 points while in Frankfurt the DAX per cent slipped
0.37 per cent to 6,975.87 points.

Elsewhere, Madrid gained 1.55 per cent, Milan 1.40 per cent, Lisbon 0.89 per cent, Swiss shares 0.71 per cent, and Amsterdam 0.15 per cent. Brussels dropped 0.28 per cent.

TOKYO - Japan's Nikkei average closed up 0.9 per cent on Wednesday after briefly hitting its highest level in almost seven months, as the dollar's rise against the yen encouraged buying after Tokyo stocks had fallen during the previous two sessions.

Foreign fund operators were keen on investing in lagging Tokyo equities but the Nikkei's advance was limited ahead of the settlement of futures and options prices on Friday, analysts said.

The Nikkei gained 91.23 points to 10,232.33, having touched an intraday high of 10,258.90, its highest level since May 18.
The broader Topix index rose 0.9 per cent to 887.39.

HONG KONG - Hong Kong shares fell 1.43 per cent and Shanghai lost 0.95 per cent on Wednesday as traders awaited a possible interest rate rise on the mainland aimed at damping down inflation.

Expectations of a rate rise have grown ahead of key economic data for November, which the mainland authorities said would be released this coming Saturday instead of the following Monday as scheduled earlier.
In Hong Kong, the benchmark Hang Seng Index shed 335.63 points to end at 23,092.52. Turnover was
$HK77.71 billion ($A10.18 billion).
In Shanghai, the Composite Index, which covers both A and B shares, was down 27.31 points at
2,848.55 on turnover of 110.2 billion yuan ($A16.7 billion).
Gold miners led the decline as the price of the precious metal slipped from a record high on Tuesday.

Page 64 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
Asian stock markets mostly fell amid expectations of the possible Chinese interest rate rise.

In other markets, Seoul closed 0.35 per cent lower, Taipei was flat, Jakarta rose 1.28 per cent, Singapore rose 0.34 per cent, Kuala Lumpur rose 0.55 per cent, Bangkok fell 1.50 per cent, or 15.64 points, and Mumbai fell 1.19 per cent.

HD      S.Korea's LG Display says it may appeal price-fixing fine
WC     269 words
PD      9 December 2010
ET       03:32 AM
SN      Agence France Presse
SC      AFPR
LA       English
CY      Copyright Agence France-Presse, 2010 All reproduction and presentation rights reserved.

LP
South Korea's LG Display Thursday admitted "wrongful acts" but said it may appeal against a huge  fine
levied by the European Commission for price-fixing.
The commission Wednesday fined the South Korean firm 215 million euros (285 million dollars) for  fixing
the prices of liquid-crystal display (LCD) panels along with five other companies between 2001 and 2006.

TD
The fine was part of penalties totalling 649 million euros levied on four Taiwanese companies and the
South Korean firm.

The leader in the  LCD business, South Korea's Samsung Electronics, was also accused of being part of the cartel. It escaped a  fine because it came forward first with information on the price-fixing.

Europe's competition watchdog accused the firms of running a  cartel that set prices, harming European buyers of televisions and computers.

LG Display, the world's second-largest supplier of LCD panels, said in a statement it "acknowledges the wrongful acts of the past" and respects the European Commission's regulatory authority.

"However, LG Display may, after careful review and consideration, appeal today's decision to the EU General Court if it finds there were procedural or substantive due process issues with the investigation."

The company said such an appeal usually lasts more than two years and the  fine could in certain circumstances be substantially reduced.

LG Display said it had taken comprehensive measures to avoid repetition of such "mistakes" and reaffirmed its commitment to highest ethical standards. It said its business would not suffer as a result of the fine.

HD      Taiwan's AU Optronics to appeal EU fine
WC     254 words
PD      9 December 2010
ET       04:00 AM
SN      Agence France Presse
SC      AFPR
LA       English
CY      Copyright Agence France-Presse, 2010 All reproduction and presentation rights reserved.

LP
Taiwan's AU Optronics (AUO) said Thursday it would appeal against a  fine imposed by the European   Commission for price-fixing  of LCD flat screens for Europe's TVs and computers.

AUO said it was planning to file an appeal against the  fine of 116.8 million euros (155 million dollars) in the General Court in Luxembourg in a statement posted on the Taiwan Stock Exchange.

TD
It expected the legal process to take at least two years and added that the European decision was not expected to affect its operations.

The European Commission on Wednesday slapped  fines totalling 649 million euros (860 million dollars) on AUO, Taiwan's Chimei InnoLux Corporation, Chunghwa Picture Tubes, HannStar Display Corporation, and South Korea's LG Display.

The other Taiwanese firms said they were considering whether to appeal while the  fines were not expected to have any major impact on their operations.

Europe's competition watchdog accused the firms of running a  cartel between October 2001 and February 2006 that fixed prices, harming European buyers of televisions and computers equipped with liquid crystal displays.

The companies held monthly meetings to agree on price ranges and minimum prices, and traded information on future production planning, capacity utilisation, pricing and other commercial conditions, the commission said.

The leader in the  LCD business, South Korea's Samsung Electronics, was also accused of being part of the cartel but escaped cash sanctions for coming forward first with information on the alleged scheme.

HD     EU slaps huge fine on South Korea, Taiwan LCD cartel
WC     620 words
PD      9 December 2010
ET      05:20 AM
SN      Agence France Presse
SC      AFPR
LA      English
CY      Copyright Agence France-Presse, 2010 All reproduction and presentation rights reserved.

LP
The European Commission has imposed 649 million euros in  fines on South Korean and Taiwanese electronics firms for secretly fixing  prices of LCD flat screens for Europe's TVs and computers.
A number of the companies indicated that they might appeal.

TD
The fines, worth 860 million dollars, were slapped Wednesday on Taiwan's AU Optronics, Chimei InnoLux Corporation, Chunghwa Picture Tubes and HannStar Display Corporation along with South Korean firm LG Display.

The leader in the  LCD business, South Korea's Samsung Electronics, was also accused of being part of the cartel but escaped cash sanctions for coming forward first with information on the alleged scheme.

"Foreign companies, like European ones, need to understand that if they want to do business in Europe they must play fair," European competition commissioner Joaquin Almunia said in a statement.

"The companies concerned knew they were breaking competition rules and took steps to conceal their illegal behaviour," he said.

Europe's competition watchdog accused the firms of running a  cartel between October 2001 and February 2006 that fixed prices, harming European buyers of televisions and computers equipped with liquid crystal displays.

The companies held monthly meetings to agree on price ranges and minimum prices, and traded information on future production planning, capacity utilisation, pricing and other commercial conditions, the commission said.

Company officials met 60 times, mainly in hotels in Taiwan, for what they dubbed "the Crystal meetings," the regulator said.

"The fact that the  cartel meetings took place outside the EU is no excuse," Almunia told a news conference, saying the group was "very well organised."

The investigation found that the companies knew they were breaking competition rules and took steps to conceal their meetings.

The commission cited a document urging everybody "to take care of security/confidentiality matters and to limit written communication."

Chimei InnoLux faces the largest  fine, 300 million euros, followed by 215 million euros against LG Display.

AU Optronics was  fined 116.8 million euros, followed by nine million euros for Chunghwa Picture Tubes and 8.1 million euros for HannStar Display.

Reacting on Thursday, South Korea's LG Display said in a statement it "acknowledges the wrongful acts of the past" and respects the  European Commission's regulatory authority.


Page 72 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
"However, LG Display may, after careful review and consideration, appeal today's decision to the EU General Court if it finds there were procedural or substantive due process issues with the investigation."

LG Display said it had taken comprehensive measures to avoid repetition of such "mistakes" and reaffirmed its commitment to high ethical standards.

Taiwan's AU Optronics (AUO) said it would appeal in the General Court in Luxembourg in a statement to the Taiwan Stock Exchange.

The other Taiwanese firms said they were considering whether to appeal, while the  fines were not expected to have a major impact on their operations.

The European Commission said Wednesday that the  cartel had a direct impact on European consumers because "the vast majority" of televisions, computer monitors and electronic notebooks with LCD panels that are sold in Europe come from Asia. The market was worth more than seven billion euros over the period that the  cartel existed.

At the same time that the  European Commission opened its investigation in late 2006 other competition regulators in the United States and Asia did the same.

LG and Chunghwa, along with Japanese firm Sharp, pleaded guilty in the United States and were  fined a total of 585 million dollars in November 2008. LG was hit with the harshest penalty, of 400 million dollars.

The European Commission cracked down on seven cartels this year, imposing nearly three billion euros in total fines.

HD     (EU) EU/COMPETITION: €648 million fine imposed  on LCD panel producers
WC    215 words
PD     9 December 2010
SN     Agence Europe
SC     AGEU
LA     English
CY     Not Available for Re-Dissemination, except as permitted by your subscriber agreement. (c) Agence
Europe, Brussels 2010. All rights reserved.

LP
Brussels, 08/12/2010 (Agence Europe) - On Wednesday 8 December, the  European Commission imposed a €648,925,000  fine on six liquid crystal display panel producers for having formed a price-fixing cartel counter to the interests of European consumers who buy television sets, computers and other products containing  LCD screens. The companies  fined are LG Display of Korea (€215 million  fine) and Taiwanese firms AU Optronics (€116.8 million), Chimei InnoLux Corporation (€300 million), Chunghwa Picture Tubes (€9.025 million) and HannStar Display Corporation (€8.1 million). The Korean company Samsung Electronics escaped a fine due to the Commission's clemency programme given that it was the first to provide information on the cartel, which lasted over 4 years (October 2001 to February 2006). Article 101 of the EU Treaty bans price-fixing  practice and all restrictive trading.

TD
Commenting on this decision, the Commission vice-president, Joaquín Almunia, responsible for competition policy pointed out that “foreign companies, like European ones, need to understand that if
they want to do business in Europe they must play fair”. He went on to add that “the companies concerned knew they were breaking competition rules and took steps to conceal their illegal behaviour”.
(O.L./transl.jl)

HD     South Korea's LG Display may appeal EU fine over LCD cartel

BY      By KELLY OLSEN CR     AP Business Writer WC    500 words
PD     9 December 2010
ET      04:23 PM
SN     Associated Press Newswires
SC     APRS
LA      English
CY     (c) 2010. The Associated Press. All Rights Reserved.

LP
SEOUL, South Korea (AP) - South Korea's LG Display said Thursday it may appeal on procedural grounds a massive European Union  fine for price fixing  even as it acknowledged it had violated competition law over several years.

The EU competition watchdog fined LG Display and four Taiwanese manufacturers euro649 million ($863 million) on Wednesday for fixing  prices on LCD panels between 2001 and 2006. One of the Taiwanese companies has already said it will challenge the ruling.

TD
A sixth LCD maker, South Korea's Samsung Electronics Co., also participated in the price  fixing  but escaped a fine because it blew the whistle on the  cartel, the European Commission said.

"LG Display acknowledges the wrongful acts of the past and respects the  European Commission's regulatory authority in this regard," the company said in a statement.
The company was fined euro215 million.

Seoul-based LG Display Co., the world's second-biggest maker of liquid crystal displays after Samsung, said it may appeal the decision "if it finds there were procedural or substantive due process issues with the investigation."
The fines targeted price-fixing  for LCD panels used in flat screens for televisions and computer monitors. Between October 2001 and February 2006, the companies met about 60 times, mostly in Taiwanese
hotels, for what they called "the Crystal meetings," the commission said. In addition to  fixing  prices, they
also exchanged information on their future production plans and other business plans, it said.

The cartel affected  LCD panel sales worth about euro7 billion in the European market, Competition Commissioner Joaquin Almunia said, and its impact on consumers was strong because most televisions and computers sold in the region come from Asia.

LG Display said the EU appeals process generally takes more than two years and that the final amount of the fine could change and even be "significantly reduced."

The company said it "has taken comprehensive measures to avoid repetition of such mistakes and reaffirms its commitment to highest ethical standards and transparency in the company's management."

In Taiwan, a spokeswoman for AU Optronics Corp. said the company would appeal the euro116.8 million fine levied against it. The three other Taiwanese companies cited in the EU judgment -- Chimei InnoLux Corp., Chunghwa Picture Tubes Ltd. and HannStar Display Corp. -- did not respond immediately to requests for comment.

Chimei received the biggest  fine, euro300 million, while Chunghwa and HannStar were  fined euro9 million and euro8.1 million, respectively.


Page 75 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
LG Display and its LG Display America Inc. unit agreed in November 2008 to pay a $400 million  fine imposed by the U.S. Justice Department in an antitrust investigation of the  LCD industry in the United States covering a price-fixing  conspiracy from 2001 to 2006. Chunghwa Picture Tubes agreed to pay $65 million for participating with LG Display and other companies.
------
Associated Press writer Peter Enav in Taipei, Taiwan, contributed to this report.

HD      DJ MARKET TALK: Asian LCD Makers Mostly Down On EU Fine
WC      222 words
PD       9 December 2010
ET       04:13 AM
SN       Dow Jones Chinese Financial Wire
SC       DJCFWE
LA       English
CY       Copyright (c) 2010, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP
0208 GMT [Dow Jones] Asian  LCD panel makers fined by the European Commission on price-fixing are mostly lower; Morgan Stanley analyst Frank Wang says charges are substantial particularly to Taiwan firms. Chimei Innolux (3481.TW), which faces the heaviest  fine at EUR300 million, is down 3.0% at NT$39.25. AU Optronics (2409.TW) with a EUR117 million  fine is down 1.1% at NT$30.45. South Korea's LG Display (034220.SE) is up 0.5% at KRW40450 despite its EUR215 million  fine. "It's a negative surprise that Chimei is  fined more than LG...Chi Mei will need to take an earnings bath in 4Q
10," says Wang. But adds, AUO's settlement should instead be viewed as a positive as the overhang is now removed, as the company had already booked the  fines as expenses in its 2009 account. Chunghwa Picture (2475.TW) which faces a much smaller EUR9 million penalty, is up 0.2% at NT$4.27 while HannStar Display (6116.TW) is down 0.5% at NT$5.61 on its EUR8 million penalty.

TD
All companies say the  fine will not have a significant impact on their operations. (aries.poon@dowjones.com)

TAIPEI (Dow Jones)--The four Taiwanese makers of liquid crystal display panels fined by the European Commission for operating a price-fixing cartel said Thursday the fines won't have a significant impact on their operations.

Chunghwa Picture Tubes Ltd. (2475.TW) said in a statement it had set aside funds for the  fines as expenses last year. The company added it hasn't decided if it will appeal the ruling.

TD
AU Optronics Corp. (2409.TW), Chimei Innolux Corp. (3481.TW) and HannStar Display Corp. (6116.TW) also confirmed that they had been  fined in separate statements.

The commission finedAU Optronics EUR117 million, Chimei InnoLux EUR300 million, Chungwa EUR9 million and HannStar EUR8 million, saying they and two Korean  LCD panel makers--Samsung Electronics Co. (005930.SE) and LG Display Co. (034220.SE)--met monthly in Taiwanese hotels to agree on prices and share other commercially sensitive information.

HD          3rd UPDATE: EU Fines Asian LCD Makers EUR649 Mln For Fixing Prices
WC         667 words
PD          9 December 2010
ET          03:36 AM
SN          Dow Jones International News
SC          DJI
LA          English
CY          (c) 2010 Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP
(Adds comments from  LCD companies, analyst, share prices.)



By Carolyn Henson
Of DOW JONES NEWSWIRES

TD
BRUSSELS (Dow Jones)--The  European Commission Wednesday fined six Asian makers of liquid crystal display screens a total of EUR649 million for operating a price-fixing  cartel for almost five years.

Samsung Electronics Co. (005930.SE) and LG Display Co. (034220.SE) of South Korea, and Taiwanese firms AU Optronics Corp. (2409.TW), Chimei Innolux Corp. (3481.TW), Chunghwa Picture Tubes (2475.TW) and HannStar Display Corp. (6116.TW) met monthly in Taiwanese hotels to agree on prices and share other commercially sensitive information, the commission said.
The cartel ran from 2001 to 2006.

The commission fined LG Display EUR215 million, AU Optronics EUR117 million, Chimei Innolux EUR300 million, Chunghwa EUR9 million and HannStar EUR8 million. Samsung received immunity from the fines for blowing the whistle on the  cartel.

The fines were based on European sales of more than EUR7 billion over the  cartel period, the commission said. The European Union has the power to  fine companies up to 10% of their global turnover for breaking its antitrust rules.

"Foreign companies, like European ones, have the obligation to respect competition rules when they do business in Europe," the EU's Competition chief Joaquin Almunia said. "The fact that the meetings took place outside of the EU is no excuse."

The companies knew their actions were illegal and took steps to conceal their gatherings, which they called "the Crystal meetings," the commissioner said. He added a  cartel document requested all the participants "to take care of confidentiality matters and to limit written communication."
There were around 60 meetings in all, Almunia said.

The cartel had a direct impact on European consumers as  LCD screens are used in televisions, computer monitors and laptops. Most of those products sold in the EU come from Asia, he added.

In setting the fines, the commission took into account the level of sales the company has in the EU and the duration of the cartel. It also reduced the  fines of some of the companies to reward their cooperation with the cartel investigation.

LG Display said in a statement Thursday it may appeal the  fine, but doesn't expect the decision to impact its business.

"LG Display acknowledges the wrongful acts of the past and respects the  European Commission's regulatory authority in this regard. However, LG Display may, after careful review and consideration,

Page 82 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
appeal today's decision to the EU General Court if it finds there were procedural or substantive due process issues with the investigation," it said in a statement.

LG Display's price-fixing  penalty follows a $400 million  fine after a price-fixing  investigation in the U.S. two years ago.

The four Taiwanese makers also said Thursday the  fines won't have a significant impact on their operations. Chunghwa said in a statement it had set aside funds for the  fines as expenses last year. The company added it hasn't decided if it will appeal the ruling. Chunghwa had also pleaded guilty to price fixing  in the same investigation.

Shares of most of the  LCD makers were down on the news. Morgan Stanley analyst Frank Wang said the charges are substantial, particularly for the Taiwan firms.

At 0232 GMT, Chimei Innolux was down 3.5% at NT$39.05; AU Optronics was 1.6% lower at NT$30.30; Chunghwa Picture Tubes was off 0.5% at NT$4.24; HannStar Display was 0.9% lower at NT$5.59; and LG Display was up 1% at KRW40,650.

"It's a negative surprise that Chimei is  fined more than LG...Chimei will need to take an earnings bath in the fourth quarter," said Wang.
-By Carolyn Henson, Dow Jones Newswires; +32 2 741 1 480; carolyn.henson@dowjones.com
--Se Young Lee in Seoul and Aries Poon in Taipei contributed to this article [ 09-12-10 0236GMT ]

CHARTING THE SENSEX
The Bombay Stock Exchange's 30-share Sensitive Index could rise to 19,760, according to charts.

TD
But Sensex has to move past major resistance at 19,850 to impart momentum to the short-term uptrend.

Until the index moves past 19,850, it would be vulnerable to a test of minor support 19,590. A fall below major support at 19,300 would indicate a reversal of the short-term bullish trend.
The National Stock Exchange's 50-share Nifty may test resistance at 5,930.

A rise above major resistance at 5,945 would lend momentum to the short-term bullish trend. While minor is at 5,885, a drop below major support at 5,850 would lend momentum to the downtrend.




US STOCKS
U.S. shares ended higher Wednesday, as surging financial stocks more than offset a broad decline across the market.

The U.S. dollar continued its recent run higher, pushing down prices of some commodities and hitting the stocks of materials, energy and industrial companies.


Page 84 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
Consumer-discretionary stocks also finished lower, weighed by a 2% decline in McDonald's. The fast-food chain led declines among Dow components after reporting same-store sales rose 4.8% in November, but fell short of analysts' estimates.

Pulling on the other side were financial stocks, fueled by gains at smaller regional banks. Lincoln National jumped 7.5%, Fifth Third Bancorp surged 6.5%, and Zions Bancorp added 5.5%. Regions Financial, Keycorp and PNC Financial Services all gained between 2.9% and 5.3%.

Morgan Stanley rose 3.2%, after the consortium of investors buying the investment bank's 34.3% stake in China International Capital all won their necessary approvals. Bank of America surged 3.7% to lead the Dow, while J.P. Morgan Chase added 2.6%.

But American International Group tumbled 3.9%, after The Wall Street Journal reported that the U.S. government is looking to sell at least $15 billion of its shares in the insurer in the first of several stock offerings to investors starting in early 2011.




ASIAN STOCKS
Asian stock markets were mostly higher Thursday, with shares in Sydney powering to a four-week high after a strong employment report while the Tokyo market continued to benefit from a lower yen.
Japan's Nikkei Stock Average, Australia's S&P/ASX 200 and South Korea's Kospi Composite were all
up while New Zealand's NZX-50 was flat. Dow Jones Industrial Average futures were 52 points higher in
screen trade.

A positive finish for U.S. stocks Wednesday aided regional sentiment, with fianancial stocks rising on the back of gains in their peers on Wall Street.

Mitsubishi UFJ FG rose 2.0% and Sumitomo Mitsui FG advanced 1.9% in Tokyo, while in Sydney ANZ Bank added 1.0% and Westpac Bank climbed 1.7%, and KB Financial Group added 0.3% and Shinhan Financial Group tacked on 0.4% in Seoul.

In Sydney, the market received a boost from a strong employment report with the benchmark S&P/ASX Index tapping a four-week high of 4747.1
Apart from banking stocks, resources were also higher. BHP Billiton rose 0.9% and Fortescue was 1.2%
higher.
In Japan, Kyocera rose 1.5%, Sony added 1.0% and Honda Motor advanced 1.1%.

In Seoul, financial and tech plays underpinned early gains. LG Display added 0.3%, reversing earlier losses that were driven by news the  European Commission had imposed a EUR215 million  fine for price fixing  between 2001-2006.
Samsung Electronics rose 0.5% and Hynix Semiconductor added 0.6%.

The Bank of Korea's decision to hold rates steady at 2.50%, as expected, didn't have any notable impact on the market.


FOREX
The euro was fetching $1.3299, from $1.3261 late Wednesday in New York, and at Y111.37 against the yen, from Y111.44. The dollar was at Y83.80, from Y84.03.


METALS
Gold futures fell Wednesday, with investors cashing in on record prices as they mulled the longer-term inflation and interest rate implications of extended U.S. tax cuts.
Spot gold was at $1,385.20 per troy ounce, up $3.90 from its New York close Wednesday.

Base metals closed mostly higher on the London Metal Exchange Wednesday after improving demand prospects stemmed the impact of a firmer U.S. dollar.


OIL SUMMARY

Page 85 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
Crude prices settled lower in U.S. trading Wednesday after the government reported U.S. stockpiles of fuel inventories rose by a larger-than-expected amount last week.
January Nymex crude oil futures, which tapped a fresh 26-month high Tuesday, were up 22 cents at
$88.92 per barrel on Globex.

HD          Taiwan LCD Makers: EU Fine Won't Have Significant Impact On Operations

TAIPEI -(Dow Jones)- The four Taiwanese makers of liquid crystal display panels fined by the European Commission for operating a price-fixing cartel said Thursday the fines won't have a significant impact on their operations.

Chunghwa Picture Tubes Ltd. (2475.TW) said in a statement it had set aside funds for the  fines as expenses last year. The company added it hasn't decided if it will appeal the ruling.

TD
AU Optronics Corp. (2409.TW), Chimei Innolux Corp. (3481.TW) and HannStar Display Corp. (6116.TW) also confirmed that they had been  fined in separate statements.

The commission finedAU Optronics EUR117 million, Chimei InnoLux EUR300 million, Chungwa EUR9 million and HannStar EUR8 million, saying they and two Korean  LCD panel makers--Samsung Electronics Co. (005930.SE) and LG Display Co. (034220.SE)--met monthly in Taiwanese hotels to agree on prices and share other commercially sensitive information.
-By Aries Poon, Dow Jones Newswires; 886-2-25022557; aries.poon@dowjones.com [ 12-08-10
2057ET ]

HD          3rd UPDATE: EU Fines Asian LCD Makers EUR649 Million  For Fixing Prices
WC         667 words
PD          9 December 2010
ET           03:51 AM
SN          Dow Jones Business News
SC          DJON
LA           English
CY          (c) 2010 Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP
(Adds comments from  LCD companies, analyst, share prices.)



By Carolyn Henson
Of DOW JONES NEWSWIRES

TD
BRUSSELS -(Dow Jones)- The  European Commission Wednesday fined six Asian makers of liquid crystal display screens a total of EUR649 million for operating a price-fixing  cartel for almost five years.

Samsung Electronics Co. (005930.SE) and LG Display Co. (034220.SE) of South Korea, and Taiwanese firms AU Optronics Corp. (2409.TW), Chimei Innolux Corp. (3481.TW), Chunghwa Picture Tubes (2475.TW) and HannStar Display Corp. (6116.TW) met monthly in Taiwanese hotels to agree on prices and share other commercially sensitive information, the commission said.
The cartel ran from 2001 to 2006.

The commission fined LG Display EUR215 million, AU Optronics EUR117 million, Chimei Innolux EUR300 million, Chunghwa EUR9 million and HannStar EUR8 million. Samsung received immunity from the fines for blowing the whistle on the  cartel.

The fines were based on European sales of more than EUR7 billion over the  cartel period, the commission said. The European Union has the power to  fine companies up to 10% of their global turnover for breaking its antitrust rules.

"Foreign companies, like European ones, have the obligation to respect competition rules when they do business in Europe," the EU's Competition chief Joaquin Almunia said. "The fact that the meetings took place outside of the EU is no excuse."

The companies knew their actions were illegal and took steps to conceal their gatherings, which they called "the Crystal meetings," the commissioner said. He added a  cartel document requested all the participants "to take care of confidentiality matters and to limit written communication."
There were around 60 meetings in all, Almunia said.

The cartel had a direct impact on European consumers as  LCD screens are used in televisions, computer monitors and laptops. Most of those products sold in the EU come from Asia, he added.

In setting the  fines, the commission took into account the level of sales the company has in the EU and the duration of the cartel. It also reduced the  fines of some of the companies to reward their cooperation with the cartel investigation.

LG Display said in a statement Thursday it may appeal the  fine, but doesn't expect the decision to impact its business.

"LG Display acknowledges the wrongful acts of the past and respects the  European Commission's regulatory authority in this regard. However, LG Display may, after careful review and consideration,

Page 105 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
appeal today's decision to the EU General Court if it finds there were procedural or substantive due process issues with the investigation," it said in a statement.
LG Display's price-fixing  penalty follows a $400 million  fine after a price-fixing  investigation in the
U.S. two years ago.

The four Taiwanese makers also said Thursday the  fines won't have a significant impact on their operations. Chunghwa said in a statement it had set aside funds for the  fines as expenses last year. The company added it hasn't decided if it will appeal the ruling. Chunghwa had also pleaded guilty to price fixing  in the same investigation.

Shares of most of the  LCD makers were down on the news. Morgan Stanley analyst Frank Wang said the charges are substantial, particularly for the Taiwan firms.

At 0232 GMT, Chimei Innolux was down 3.5% at NT$39.05; AU Optronics was 1.6% lower at NT$30.30; Chunghwa Picture Tubes was off 0.5% at NT$4.24; HannStar Display was 0.9% lower at NT$5.59; and LG Display was up 1% at KRW40,650.

"It's a negative surprise that Chimei is  fined more than LG...Chimei will need to take an earnings bath in the fourth quarter," said Wang.
-By Carolyn Henson, Dow Jones Newswires; +32 2 741 1 480; carolyn.henson@dowjones.com
--Se Young Lee in Seoul and Aries Poon in Taipei contributed to this article [ 12-08-10 2151ET ]

IN            i3302 : Computers/Electronics | i34531 : Semiconductors | iindstrls : Industrials | ielec : Electronics | i34532 : Components for Electronic Goods | i3454 : Electronic Consumer Goods | icnp : Consumer Products | idurhg : Durable Household Products | ihome : Home Electronics/Appliances

HD                 EU imposes  fines on local firms;  CRYSTAL MEETINGS:European  investigation found the firms knew they were engaging  in illegal behavior  and urged participants to take care of confidentiality
CR                 Staff writer, with AFP and CNA, BRUSSELS and TAIPEI
WC                472 words
PD                 9 December 2010
SN                 Taipei Times
SC                 TAIP
LA                  English
CY                 © Copyright 2010 The Taipei Times. All rights reserved.

LP
The European Commission yesterday imposed 649 million euros (US$860 million) in fines on four Taiwanese and one South Korean maker of  LCD flat screens for running a price-fixing  cartel.
Taiwans AU Optronics Corp, Chimei Innolux Corp, Chunghwa Picture Tubes Ltd and HannStar
Display Corp were hit with  fines along with South Korean firm LG Display Co.

TD
South Koreas Samsung Electronics Co was also accused of being a part of the  cartel, but avoided a fine for being the first to provide information on the alleged scheme.

Europes competition watchdog accused the firms of running a  cartel between October 2001 and February 2006 that fixed prices, harming European buyers of televisions and computers equipped with the  LCD component.

The companies held monthly meetings to agree on price ranges and minimum prices and trade information on future production planning, capacity utilization, pricing and other commercial conditions, the commission said.

Company officials met 60 times, mainly in hotels in Taiwan, for what they dubbed the Crystal meetings, the regulator said.

The investigation found that the companies knew they were breaking competition rules and took steps to conceal their meetings.

The commission cited a document urging everybody to take care of security [and] confidentiality matters and to limit written communication.

Chimei Innolux received the largest  fine, 300 million euros, followed by 215 million euros for LG Display.
AU Optronics was  fined 116.8 million euros, followed by 9 -million euros for Chunghwa Picture
Tubes and 8.1 million euros for HannStar Display.

Foreign companies, like European ones, need to understand that if they want to do business in Europe they must play fair, European Commissioner for Competition Joaquin Almunia said in a statement.

The companies concerned knew they were breaking competition rules and took steps to conceal their illegal behaviour, he said.

Earlier yesterday in Taipei, the Ministry of Economic Affairs (MOEA) expressed concerns over potential fines the European Commission could slap on several Taiwanese  LCD makers for alleged price fixing  and said the government would provide any assistance necessary.

Industrial Development Bureau Director-General Woody Duh said as long as the accused companies needed assistance when facing disciplinary action, the government would do its best to help them.
Page 109 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
Duh said the ministry has contacted the four local companies and offered its help based on the decision laid down by the  European Commission.
The damage is higher than we thought, Chimei Innolux spokesman Eddie Chen told the Taipei
Times by telephone last night.

The company will book the payment in its fourth-quarter financial statement after receiving the formal ruling, Chen said.
Additional reporting by Lisa Wang

HD      European Commission fines LCD manufacturers £542m
BY      Dan Worth
WC     333 words
PD      9 December 2010
SN      VNUNet United Kingdom
SC      VNUN
LA      English
CY      Copyright 2010 VNU Business Publications. All Rights Reserved.

LP
Samsung and LG among those found guilty of price-fixing

Six major LCD panel producers have been fined a total of €648m (£542m) by the  European                   Commission (EC) for operating a price-fixing  cartel that affected the cost of televisions, computer screens and other technologies.

TD
An EC investigation found that Samsung, LG, AU Optronics, Chimei InnoLux Corporation, Chunghwa Picture Tubes and HannStar Display Corporation agreed price ranges and minimum prices, and exchanged information on future production plans and capacity utilisation, over a period of four years.

The companies convened around 60 monthly gatherings in Taiwan in what they called "the crystal meetings".

The EC said that the manufacturers were fully aware that the discussions broke competition rules, and the investigation uncovered a document that requested the firms to "take care of security/confidentiality matters and to limit written communication".

Samsung avoided a  fine, however, as it received full immunity under the EC's 2002 Leniency Notice for bringing the cartel to the EC's attention and helping to prove the infringement.

LG received a 50 per cent reduction for its co-operation, but was still  fined €215m (€180m), while AU Optronics received a 20 per cent reduction, resulting in a  fine of €116m (£97m).

Chimei was the firm hardest hit by the EC's decision, being forced to pay €300m (£251m), and HannStar was fined €8.1m (£6.69m) and Chunghwa €9m (£7.5m).

Joaquín Almunia, EC vice president in charge of competition policy, hopes that the ruling will send a message to other companies about the tough stance taken against price-fixing.

"Foreign companies, like European ones, need to understand that, if they want to do business in Europe, they must play fair. The companies concerned knew they were breaking competition rules and took steps to conceal their illegal behaviour," he said.

"The only understanding we will show is for those that come forward to denounce a  cartel and help prove its existence."

HD      EU Slaps Fine on South Korean and Taiwanese LCD-Panel Makers
BY       Sarah McDowall
WC      246 words
PD       9 December 2010
SN       IHS Global Insight Daily Analysis
SC       WDAN
LA       English
CY       Copyright 2010, IHS Global Insight Limited. All Rights Reserved.

LP
The European Commission yesterday slapped penalties on five South Korean and Taiwanese firms for fixing  the prices of liquid-crystal display panels. The five companies involved included Taiwan's Chimei Innolux, Chunghwa Picture Tubes, HannStar Display, and AU Optronics, as well as South Korea's LG Display. Chimei Innolux has been ordered to pay the largest  fine of US$400 million, while LG Display must pay the second largest sum of US$286 million. Samsung, the largest  LCD-maker in the world, dodged the penalty after reporting the  cartel to the regulatory authorities. Speaking in Brussels today, EU Competition Commissioner Joaquin Alumnia said that, "foreign companies, like European ones, have an obligation to respect competition rules when they do business in Europe". The price-fixing  activity occurred between October 2001 and February 2006. The companies held monthly meetings to agree on pricing and production planning.

TD
Responding to the announcement in a statement to the Taiwan Stock Exchange, AU Optronics has said that it will appeal the ruling in the General Court in Luxembourg.Significance: The price-fixing cartel directly affected consumers in Europe, as the  LCD screens are the main components of flat monitors used in computers, notebooks, and televisions. The  European Commission has imposed fines totalling more than US$4 billion this year in similar cases, with this latest South Korea/Taiwan case being the seventh dealt with by Brussels in 2010.

HD            LG Display may appeal against EU fines
WC           255 words
PD            9 December 2010
SN            Yonhap English News
SC            YONH
LA             English
CY            © Copyright 2010 Yonhap News Agency. All rights reserved.

LP
SEOUL, Dec. 9 (Yonhap) -- LG Display Co., the world's second-largest supplier of liquid-crystal display (LCD) panels, said Thursday that it may lodge an appeal against the  European                     Commission's (EC) decision to  fine the company for price  fixing.

On Wednesday, the European Union's executive body  fined LG Display 215 million euros (US$285 million) for fixing LCD panel prices with five other companies between 2001 and 2006.

TD
"We admit our wrongful acts of the past and we respect the EC's regulatory authority in this regard," the South Korean company said in a statement.

"However, after a careful review, if we come to a conclusion that there are problems in the EC's investigation process or in the result, we may lodge an appeal to the EU General Court," it added.

LG Display added that the legal procedures in the EU General Court usually take more than 2 years, and that there is a possibility that the  fine gets slashed down.  LCD panels are used for flat-screen TVs, computer monitors and mobile phones.
The EU imposed a total 648.9 million euros of  fines on Asian LCD makers, including Chi Mei
Optoelectronics Corp. and AU Optronics Corp.

Samsung Electronics Co., the world's largest LCD supplier, which was among the companies in the price-fixing cartel, was exempted from the fine because it informed the EU of the  cartel, according to media reports.
ylee@yna.co.kr

HD      EU fines 4 Taiwanese LCD makers EUR 433.93 mln for cartel

Dec. 9, 2010 (China Knowledge) - The  European Commission, the EU's competition watchdog, said yesterday that it  fined four Taiwanese companies a total of EUR 433.93 million for  fixing  prices on liquid crystal display panels between 2001 and 2006. Chimei Innolux Corp, which resulted from the merger of Taiwan-based display makers Chi Mei Optoelectronics Co, Innolux Display Co and TPO Displays Co, received the biggest  fine of EUR 300 million, while AU Optronics, the world's third-largest maker of  LCD panels, was fined EUR 116.8 million. Two smaller Taiwanese, Chunghwa Picture Tubes and HannStar Display Corp, received  fines of EUR 9.02 million and EUR 8.1 million, respectively. All of the four Taiwanese firms have confirmed the fines, which are said not to have a significant impact on their operations. The commission also fined two South Korean firms, Samsung Electronics Co and LG Display Co.

TD
LG Display has to pay EUR 215 million of  fine, while Samsung Samsung was given full immunity from fines under the commission's leniency programme, as it was the first to provide information about the cartel.

HD        EU fines flat panel makers for price fixing
BY        The China Post Staff
WC       362 words
PD        9 December 2010
SN        The China Post
SC        CHIPOS
LA         English
CY        (c) 2010 The China Post. All Rights Reserved

LP
European Union regulators yesterday announced  fines for the South Korea-based LG Display,
Taiwan-based Chi Mei Optoelectronics Corp and three other Taiwanese firms totaling 649 million euros
(US$858 million, NT$25.9 billion) for  fixing  prices of display panels used in consumer devices.
Samsung Electronics, the world's largest flat panel maker, was not charged since it alerted the
European Commission to the price-fixing  practices.

TD
Chi Mei, now part of Chi Mei Innolux, Taiwan's largest  LCD maker, was handed the biggest  fine of 300 million euros. The punishment came after the company paid US$220 million in  fines last year in the U.S. over charges of price-fixing.
LG Display, the world's No. 2 LCD maker, Taiwanese firms AU Optronics, Chunghwa Picture Tubes and
HannStar Display Corp were also fined.

The EU antitrust watchdog  European Commission charged the firms with breaching EU laws on restrictive business practices in July last year. Other regulators around the world have also investigated the sector.

In the U.S. Department of Justice antitrust investigation, eight companies, including LG Display, Chi Mei, Chunghwa Picture Tubes, Sharp and Hitachi Displays, have pleaded guilty and paid more than US$890 million (NT$2.81 billion) in criminal  fines for price-fixing.  AU Optronics Corp., its U.S. subsidiary and six of its executives were also named in the indictment but decided to contest the charge.
The Ministry of Economic Affairs (MOEA) earlier vowed to provide any assistance necessary to several
Taiwanese flat panel makers  fined by the European Commission over price fixing.

Duh Tyzz-jiun, director-general of the MOEA's Industrial Development Bureau said that the government would do its best to assist the companies concerned if they require help when facing the EU's disciplinary action.

Duh said the MOEA has made contact with the four local companies to extend its offer of assistance that will be based on the decision laid down by the  European Commission.

The companies have told the ministry they will carefully study the EU's decision to gauge the impact on them, he said.

0011 GMT [Dow Jones] Japan's government revises upward the nation's July-September GDP growth rate to an annualized 4.5% from a preliminary 3.9%, saying consumption and capex turned out to be stronger than initially thought; the on-quarter growth rate rises to 1.1% from a prior estimate of 0.9%. The results were better than the expectations of economists polled by Dow Jones, Nikkei that centered on GDP being revised to a 4.1% annualized increase and 1.0% on-quarter growth. But the data are not likely to dispel pessimism over Japan's economic outlook, because the 3Q figures are too old and many expect a contraction in 4Q due to slowing exports. (takashi.nakamichi@dowjones.com)

0042 GMT [Dow Jones] USD/KRW is lower at 1,140.0, vs 1,146.0 late yesterday in Seoul, amid Kospi's
0.6% rise; the pair is testing support at the current level. But not many in the market expect steep falls
ahead of BOK's rate decision due around 0100 GMT, with the central bank widely expected to stand pat,
traders say. "The dollar's surge yesterday to levels above KRW1,140, shows that the market still remains
sensitive to geopolical risks," which is another factor that will keep the pair from falling sharply, says a
local bank trader. Support is pegged at 1,135.0. But another trader cautions over the chance of a rate
hike; "currently, a possible rate hike isn't priced into the won at all. So, a surprise hike could lead to a
really sharp fall in the dollar/won." (min-jeong.lee@dowjones.com)

0011 GMT [Dow Jones] Japan's government revises upward the nation's July-September GDP growth rate to an annualized 4.5% from a preliminary 3.9%, saying consumption and capex turned out to be stronger than initially thought; the on-quarter growth rate rises to 1.1% from a prior estimate of 0.9%. The results were better than the expectations of economists polled by Dow Jones, Nikkei that centered on GDP being revised to a 4.1% annualized increase and 1.0% on-quarter growth. But the data are not likely to dispel pessimism over Japan's economic outlook, because the 3Q figures are too old and many expect a contraction in 4Q due to slowing exports. (takashi.nakamichi@dowjones.com)

0008 GMT [Dow Jones] Wall Street's modest gains overnight may help underpin Singapore shares and keep the STI above the 3200 level; the index closed +0.3% at 3202.80 yesterday, above 3200 for the first time since Nov. 18. Resistance is likely at 3230 (Nov. 19 high), while this week's current 3164 low is expected to provide support on any downside. "The STI may still be able to head higher for the rest of December, but the climb is likely to be slow and gradual as there's really not much going on, especially at this time of the year, to cause any excitement in the market," says a local house trader. Pacific Andes Resources Development (P11.SG) may be in focus as the frozen fish supplier expands its seafood business by acquiring a 19.76% stake in ASX-listed Tassal Group (TGR.AU) for S$67 million; the stock ended flat at S$0.34 yesterday. (frankie.ho@dowjones.com)

0000 GMT [Dow Jones] Korea treasury bonds, bond futures may fall in early trade, tracking weaker U.S. Treasurys overnight, though any steep falls unlikely ahead of the BOK's rate decision due around 0100
GMT; all 14 economists, fixed-income analysts polled by Dow Jones expect the BOK to stand pat at
2.50% after its 25-bp hike last month. "The market may find some comfort, if the central bank actually

decision, says a local bank trader. Adds, "but I think the BOK will likely touch on how it will have to
resume hiking rates next year," which could weigh on bond sentiment. Focus on how 3-year bonds will
perform, following their volatile swings of late amid lingering concerns over supply shortage issues for
that tenor. Tips 3-year yield in 3.00%-3.15% range vs 3.08% yesterday. (min-jeong.lee@dowjones.com)

$88.63/bbl on Globex. (jerry.tan@dowjones.com)

0048 GMT [Dow Jones] Lead 10-year JGB futures open slightly lower, hovering around Wednesday's closing level in cautious trade; now up 0.10 at 140.20. The contract briefly slips below 140.00 for the first time since May 20, while cash 10-year bond yield climbs to 1.250% for the first time since June 4 vs
1.240% on Wednesday. With U.S. Treasurys extending their fall and cash JGB yields rising to fresh
6-month highs, investors are become nervous about the possibility of continued moves by major
institutional players to shift money away from the safe-haven investment into riskier assets, analysts say.
"While there is no significant change in fundamentals, moves to adjust positions and reduce the risk
exposure (due to market volatility) will continue" ahead of the holiday season, says Mitsubishi UFJ
Morgan Stanley chief strategist Jun Ishii. (kazuhiro.shimamura@dowjones.com)

TD
0044 GMT [Dow Jones] Australia's economy continued to create jobs at a stellar pace in November, signaling that the underlying strength of economic growth is much stronger than suggested by some recent data, and will likely keep the RBA on watch for inflationary pressures in early 2011. November employment grew 54,600 vs consensus rise of 19,100 over the month and unemployment fell to an
as-expected 5.2% vs 5.4% in October; more people entered the workforce -- a solid indicator of rising confidence in the economy. AUD/USD rises by close to half a U.S. cent; now 0.9835 vs 0.09790 before the data. (james.glynn@dowjones.com)
0042 GMT [Dow Jones] USD/KRW is lower at 1,140.0, vs 1,146.0 late yesterday in Seoul, amid Kospi's
0.6% rise; the pair is testing support at the current level. But not many in the market expect steep falls
ahead of BOK's rate decision due around 0100 GMT, with the central bank widely expected to stand pat,
traders say. "The dollar's surge yesterday to levels above KRW1,140, shows that the market still remains
sensitive to geopolical risks," which is another factor that will keep the pair from falling sharply, says a
local bank trader. Support is pegged at 1,135.0. But another trader cautions over the chance of a rate
hike; "currently, a possible rate hike isn't priced into the won at all. So, a surprise hike could lead to a
really sharp fall in the dollar/won." (min-jeong.lee@dowjones.com)

0040 GMT [Dow Jones] The Nikkei Stock Average was up 0.5% at 10,287.17 after hitting a fresh seven-month intraday high of 10,298.25, as exporters extended gains on a weaker yen (USD/JPY at
84.10 and EUR/JPY at 111.39) and an overnight rise in U.S. stocks. Market reaction has been limited after the Japanese government revised upward its July-September GDP growth rate to an annualized
4.5% versus a preliminary 3.9%. "It is difficult to react positively since we can anticipate a slowdown in the October to December quarter," says Cosmo Securities equity strategist Toshikazu Horiuchi. He puts today's index range at 10,200-10,400, noting there may be some volatility before options and futures settlement tomorrow. 22/33 Topix subindexes higher; Kyocera (6971.TO) up 1.5% at Y8,820, Honda Motor (7267.TO) up 1.1% at Y3,170. Banks outperform following overnight gains in U.S. financial stocks; Mitsubishi UFJ FG (8306.TO) up 2.0% at Y410 and Sumitomo Mitsui FG (8316.TO) up 1.9% at Y2,669. TDK (6762.TO) up 2.3% at Y5,770 on a Nikkei report that the company will aim for a double-digit operating profit margin in FY 2011. (kana.inagaki@dowjones.com)

HD      MARKET TALK: Flat-Panel TVs May Limit Japan 4Q GDP Pain - MRI WC     1,734 words
PD      9 December 2010
ET      03:08 AM
SN      Dow Jones Capital Markets Report
SC      CM
LA       English
CY      (c) 2010 Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP



Contact us in Singapore. 65 64154 140; MarketTalk@dowjones.com


0208 GMT [Dow Jones] The upward revision to Japan's 3Q real GDP doesn't change expectations for contraction in 4Q due in part to a fall-off in demand after the end of government subsidies for fuel-efficient cars, but the recently brisk demand for flat-panel TVs and other electronics may limit the pain, says Hirokata Kusaba, senior economist at Mizuho Research Institute. The government will cut incentives by half in December for environmentally friendly electric appliances, which should lead to another burst of rush-buying. "This last-minute demand, in particular the strong demand for flat-panel TVs, should help make up for some of the drop in consumption in the October-December quarter expected due to the earlier end of the 'eco-car' subsidies." (andrew.monahan@dowjones.com)

TD
0208 GMT [Dow Jones] Asian  LCD panel makers fined by the European Commission on price-fixing are mostly lower; Morgan Stanley analyst Frank Wang says charges are substantial particularly to Taiwan firms. Chimei Innolux (3481.TW), which faces the heaviest fine at EUR300 million, is down 3.0% at NT$39.25. AU Optronics (2409.TW) with a EUR117 million fine is down 1.1% at NT$30.45. South
Korea's LG Display (034220.SE) is up 0.5% at KRW40450 despite its EUR215 million  fine. "It's a negative surprise that Chimei is  fined more than LG...Chi Mei will need to take an earnings bath in 4Q
10," says Wang. But adds, AUO's settlement should instead be viewed as a positive as the overhang is now removed, as the company had already booked the  fines as expenses in its 2009 account. Chunghwa Picture (2475.TW) which faces a much smaller EUR9 million penalty, is up 0.2% at NT$4.27 while HannStar Display (6116.TW) is down 0.5% at NT$5.61 on its EUR8 million penalty. All companies say the fine will not have a significant impact on their operations. (aries.poon@dowjones.com)

0202 GMT [Dow Jones] EUR/USD gets a bump from stronger-than-expected Australia jobs data, as the positive surprise helps risk-sensitive assets such as the common currency, says Yuichiro Harada, senior FX dealer at Mizuho Corporate Bank. "The strong Australian jobs data was a trigger to buy the euro." Adds that many investors may not find U.S. Treasury yield rises to be a compelling reason to sell the pair as "the trend of higher yields is rather now a global phenomenon, not just a local U.S. issue, and that diminishes the dollar-positive impact." Says EUR/USD may target 1.3400 later in the global day, with
further help coming from "a sense that Ireland is no longer as much in the spotlight and that the European sovereign debt concerns are receding a little for now." Pair last at 1.3305, up from its earlier low at
1.3244.(andrew.monahan@dowjones.com)

0201 GMT [Dow Jones] China shares are lower as investors are concerned the PBOC could hike the reserve requirement ratio or the benchmark interest rate (in the coming days) to curb inflation after suspending the 3-year bill sale. The Shanghai Composite Index is down 0.3% at 2841.35 and it's tipped to hover around current level for the rest of the session. "The Shanghai index could rebound next week if the central bank doesn't launch any (additional tightening) measures after the November data," says Li Lei at Gold State Securities. Among most active stocks, China Vanke (000002.SZ) down 1.3% at CNY8.38, Poly Real Estate Group (600048,SH) down 1.7% at CNY12.49, China Everbright Bank (601818.SH) down 1.6% at CNY3.73. Shenzhen index is down 0.7% at 1296.49. (wynne.wang@dowjones.com)

But typically when you have a good December you see a pull back in January," says Yuanta head of research John Brebeck. Adds may be premature for the market to sustain the 8800-8900 level. 0151 GMT [Dow Jones] Singapore shares are slightly higher, with the STI +0.2% at 3208.02, tracking modest gains in other Asian markets after U.S. stocks end higher. Gainers outnumber decliners 2 to 1, although buying conviction is as low as volumes are light. The STI is likely to face resistance at 3230 (November 19 high). 8 consecutive sessions now. December open interest increases 574 lots to 94,073. (robert.li@dowjones.com)

0146 GMT [Dow Jones] Southeast Australian wheat crops were hit by another deluge overnight, causing widespread flooding, likely further damaging milling wheat and resulting in quality downgrades and so increasing feed grade supplies. Bureau of Meteorology shows northeast Victoria and southwest slopes and Riverina districts of New South Wales were worst hit by overnight falls, with West Wyalong receiving
62 mm in 24 hours to 9 a.m., while Wagga Wagga, Yarrawonga and Lake Cargelligo all received 58 mm, and Coolamon 55 mm. ASX milling wheat futures deliverable in New South Wales have soared since late November, with this latest rainfall on ripe crops likely to further support these contracts. January is quoted A$349/A$355 a metric ton, compared with yesterday's close at A$351, while March is quoted at A$322/A$359, compared with yesterday's close at A$335. (ray.brindal@dowjones.com)

A high yield "should offset other negative factors," says Mitsubishi UFJ Morgan Stanley strategist Katsutoshi Inadome. Coupon on the new issue is set at 0.5% vs 0.3% in the last auction; the 5-year yield is now at 0.525%. But some analysts are still calling for caution, considering the fact that the amount of the issue is large at Y2.4

HD      MARKET TALK: NZ Card Spending  Likely To Be Subdued In 2011 -GS WC     1,718 words

0209 GMT [Dow Jones] Statistics NZ data shows total retail spending on electronic cards in November was +1.4% on-month, +6.1% on-year, but a subdued consumer backdrop is still likely for majority of
2011, says Goldman Sachs Economist Philip Borkin; "The value of electronic card transaction was reasonable in November, however, we suspect price rises for fuel and other necessities is partly to blame." Borkin says while the risk is that households slow their pace of deleveraging given the progress made to date and hence more consumption growth results, he reckons this is unlikely due to the forecast fall in house prices; "If house prices were to stabilise and begin to rise, we would become more optimistic on the prospects for household consumption and hence the economy itself." (lucy.craymer@dowjones.com)

0215 GMT [Dow Jones] Singapore's 4Q GDP is likely to rebound 10.5% on-quarter, seasonally-adjusted, annualized vs 18.7% contraction in 3Q; 2010 GDP likely +15.2% on-year, above government expectations, Credit Suisse says in a report. Adds, "government revenues are likely to come in much higher than expected, thanks in part to the surge in betting revenues from the two new casinos, stamp duties from property transactions, and higher goods and services tax revenues from the rebound in retail sales." House expects a fiscal surplus at 0.8% of GDP in FY 2010 vs a 1.0% deficit budgeted. With stronger economic growth, the Monetary Authority of Singapore is likely to remain on a "tightening bias," report says. (gaurav.raghuvanshi@dowjones.com)

0221 GMT [Dow Jones] China government bonds are flat after the PBOC leaves the yield on the 3-month bills unchanged at 1.8131% in its regular open market operation; the move cools expectations of an imminent interest rate hike. A Shenzhen-based trader with a local fund says the unchanged rate on the
bill sale comes after the PBOC scraps a regular auction of 3-year bonds in today's OMO, and suggests "the central bank wants to ensure money market liquidity won't be too tight after two consecutive reserve requirement ratio increases last month." Shanghai Stock Exchange government bond index is at 126.19, unchanged from its last close, and is tipped to consolidate in a narrow 126.15-126.25 range for the rest of the session. (ming.wang@dowjones.com)

TD
0217 GMT [Dow Jones] Indonesia shares are likely to open higher, helped by steady IDR and gains in many Asian markets, traders say. Expect index to top psychological 3800 level after shares ended +1.2% at record high of 3769.993 yesterday; "it looks like the main index is on the right track to test the 3800 level amid hopes for healthy inflows," says trader at First Asia Capital. Foreigners were net buyers of IDR193 billion worth of shares yesterday. Nickel producer Inco (INCO.JK) may rise on higher commodity prices and coal producer Bumi (BUMI.JK) may gain as its unit Bumi Resources Minerals (BRMS.JK)
starts its maiden trade today; the new IPO is likely to rise over 10% on debut.(edhi.pranasidhi@dowjones.com)

0215 GMT [Dow Jones] Singapore's 4Q GDP is likely to rebound 10.5% on-quarter, seasonally-adjusted, annualized vs 18.7% contraction in 3Q; 2010 GDP likely +15.2% on-year, above government expectations, Credit Suisse says in a report. Adds, "government revenues are likely to come in much higher than expected, thanks in part to the surge in betting revenues from the two new casinos, stamp duties from property transactions, and higher goods and services tax revenues from the rebound in retail sales." House expects a fiscal surplus at 0.8% of GDP in FY 2010 vs a 1.0% deficit budgeted. With stronger economic growth, the Monetary Authority of Singapore is likely to remain on a "tightening bias," report says. (gaurav.raghuvanshi@dowjones.com)

0209 GMT [Dow Jones] Statistics NZ data shows total retail spending on electronic cards in November was +1.4% on-month, +6.1% on-year, but a subdued consumer backdrop is still likely for majority of
2011, says Goldman Sachs Economist Philip Borkin; "The value of electronic card transaction was reasonable in November, however, we suspect price rises for fuel and other necessities is partly to blame." Borkin says while the risk is that households slow their pace of deleveraging given the progress made to date and hence more consumption growth results, he reckons this is unlikely due to the forecast fall in house prices; "If house prices were to stabilise and begin to rise, we would become more optimistic on the prospects for household consumption and hence the economy itself." (lucy.craymer@dowjones.com)

0208 GMT [Dow Jones] The upward revision to Japan's 3Q real GDP doesn't change expectations for contraction in 4Q due in part to a fall-off in demand after the end of government subsidies for fuel-efficient cars, but the recently brisk demand for flat-panel TVs and other electronics may limit the pain, says Hirokata Kusaba, senior economist at Mizuho Research Institute. The government will cut incentives by

Page 146 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
half in December for environmentally friendly electric appliances, which should lead to another burst of rush-buying. "This last-minute demand, in particular the strong demand for flat-panel TVs, should help make up for some of the drop in consumption in the October-December quarter expected due to the earlier end of the 'eco-car' subsidies." (andrew.monahan@dowjones.com)

0208 GMT [Dow Jones] Asian  LCD panel makers fined by the European Commission on price-fixing are mostly lower; Morgan Stanley analyst Frank Wang says charges are substantial particularly to Taiwan firms. Chimei Innolux (3481.TW), which faces the heaviest fine at EUR300 million, is down 3.0% at NT$39.25. AU Optronics (2409.TW) with a EUR117 million fine is down 1.1% at NT$30.45. South
Korea's LG Display (034220.SE) is up 0.5% at KRW40450 despite its EUR215 million  fine. "It's a negative surprise that Chimei is  fined more than LG...Chi Mei will need to take an earnings bath in 4Q
10," says Wang. But adds, AUO's settlement should instead be viewed as a positive as the overhang is now removed, as the company had already booked the  fines as expenses in its 2009 account. Chunghwa Picture (2475.TW) which faces a much smaller EUR9 million penalty, is up 0.2% at NT$4.27 while HannStar Display (6116.TW) is down 0.5% at NT$5.61 on its EUR8 million penalty. All companies say the fine will not have a significant impact on their operations. (aries.poon@dowjones.com)

0202 GMT [Dow Jones] EUR/USD gets a bump from stronger-than-expected Australia jobs data, as the positive surprise helps risk-sensitive assets such as the common currency, says Yuichiro Harada, senior FX dealer at Mizuho Corporate Bank. "The strong Australian jobs data was a trigger to buy the euro." Adds that many investors may not find U.S. Treasury yield rises to be a compelling reason to sell the pair as "the trend of higher yields is rather now a global phenomenon, not just a local U.S. issue, and that diminishes the dollar-positive impact." Says EUR/USD may target 1.3400 later in the global day, with
further help coming from "a sense that Ireland is no longer as much in the spotlight and that the European sovereign debt concerns are receding a little for now." Pair last at 1.3305, up from its earlier low at
1.3244.(andrew.monahan@dowjones.com)

will act to stabilize prices of goods and commodities in the local market. "Investor sentiment is weak
because concerns over high inflation remain and banks also continue to increase rates which will hurt
companies' profitability this month," says ACB Securities analyst. Among decliners, Ocean Group
(OGC.VH) down 1.7% at VND23,300, Vietcombank (VCB.VH) down 1.6% at VND31,300 and Itaco
(ITA.VH) down 2.8% at VND14,100. Tips immediate support at 450. (phammuoi.nguyen@dowjones.com)

0221 GMT [Dow Jones] China government bonds are flat after the PBOC leaves the yield on the 3-month bills unchanged at 1.8131% in its regular open market operation; the move cools expectations of an imminent interest rate hike. A Shenzhen-based trader with a local fund says the unchanged rate on the
bill sale comes after the PBOC scraps a regular auction of 3-year bonds in today's OMO, and suggests "the central bank wants to ensure money market liquidity won't be too tight after two consecutive reserve requirement ratio increases last month." Shanghai Stock Exchange government bond index is at 126.19, unchanged from its last close, and is tipped to consolidate in a narrow 126.15-126.25 range for the rest of the session. (ming.wang@dowjones.com)

0217 GMT [Dow Jones] Indonesia shares are likely to open higher, helped by steady IDR and gains in many Asian markets, traders say. Expect index to top psychological 3800 level after shares ended +1.2% at record high of 3769.993 yesterday; "it looks like the main index is on the right track to test the 3800 level amid hopes for healthy inflows," says trader at First Asia Capital. Foreigners were net buyers of IDR193 billion worth of shares yesterday. Nickel producer Inco (INCO.JK) may rise on higher commodity prices and coal producer Bumi (BUMI.JK) may gain as its unit Bumi Resources Minerals (BRMS.JK)


Page 152 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
starts its maiden trade today; the new IPO is likely to rise over 10% on debut.(edhi.pranasidhi@dowjones.com)

0215 GMT [Dow Jones] Singapore's 4Q GDP is likely to rebound 10.5% on-quarter, seasonally-adjusted, annualized vs 18.7% contraction in 3Q; 2010 GDP likely +15.2% on-year, above government expectations, Credit Suisse says in a report. Adds, "government revenues are likely to come in much higher than expected, thanks in part to the surge in betting revenues from the two new casinos, stamp duties from property transactions, and higher goods and services tax revenues from the rebound in retail sales." House expects a fiscal surplus at 0.8% of GDP in FY 2010 vs a 1.0% deficit budgeted. With stronger economic growth, the Monetary Authority of Singapore is likely to remain on a "tightening bias," report says. (gaurav.raghuvanshi@dowjones.com)

0209 GMT [Dow Jones] Statistics NZ data shows total retail spending on electronic cards in November was +1.4% on-month, +6.1% on-year, but a subdued consumer backdrop is still likely for majority of
2011, says Goldman Sachs Economist Philip Borkin; "The value of electronic card transaction was reasonable in November, however, we suspect price rises for fuel and other necessities is partly to blame." Borkin says while the risk is that households slow their pace of deleveraging given the progress made to date and hence more consumption growth results, he reckons this is unlikely due to the forecast fall in house prices; "If house prices were to stabilise and begin to rise, we would become more optimistic on the prospects for household consumption and hence the economy itself." (lucy.craymer@dowjones.com)

0208 GMT [Dow Jones] The upward revision to Japan's 3Q real GDP doesn't change expectations for contraction in 4Q due in part to a fall-off in demand after the end of government subsidies for fuel-efficient cars, but the recently brisk demand for flat-panel TVs and other electronics may limit the pain, says Hirokata Kusaba, senior economist at Mizuho Research Institute. The government will cut incentives by half in December for environmentally friendly electric appliances, which should lead to another burst of rush-buying. "This last-minute demand, in particular the strong demand for flat-panel TVs, should help make up for some of the drop in consumption in the October-December quarter expected due to the earlier end of the 'eco-car' subsidies." (andrew.monahan@dowjones.com)

0208 GMT [Dow Jones] Asian  LCD panel makers fined by the European Commission on price-fixing are mostly lower; Morgan Stanley analyst Frank Wang says charges are substantial particularly to Taiwan firms. Chimei Innolux (3481.TW), which faces the heaviest fine at EUR300 million, is down 3.0% at NT$39.25. AU Optronics (2409.TW) with a EUR117 million fine is down 1.1% at NT$30.45. South
Korea's LG Display (034220.SE) is up 0.5% at KRW40450 despite its EUR215 million  fine. "It's a negative surprise that Chimei is  fined more than LG...Chi Mei will need to take an earnings bath in 4Q
10," says Wang. But adds, AUO's settlement should instead be viewed as a positive as the overhang is now removed, as the company had already booked the  fines as expenses in its 2009 account. Chunghwa Picture (2475.TW) which faces a much smaller EUR9 million penalty, is up 0.2% at NT$4.27 while HannStar Display (6116.TW) is down 0.5% at NT$5.61 on its EUR8 million penalty. All companies say the fine will not have a significant impact on their operations. (aries.poon@dowjones.com)

0202 GMT [Dow Jones] EUR/USD gets a bump from stronger-than-expected Australia jobs data, as the positive surprise helps risk-sensitive assets such as the common currency, says Yuichiro Harada, senior FX dealer at Mizuho Corporate Bank. "The strong Australian jobs data was a trigger to buy the euro." Adds that many investors may not find U.S. Treasury yield rises to be a compelling reason to sell the pair as "the trend of higher yields is rather now a global phenomenon, not just a local U.S. issue, and that diminishes the dollar-positive impact." Says EUR/USD may target 1.3400 later in the global day, with
further help coming from "a sense that Ireland is no longer as much in the spotlight and that the European sovereign debt concerns are receding a little for now." Pair last at 1.3305, up from its earlier low at
1.3244.(andrew.monahan@dowjones.com)

0201 GMT [Dow Jones] China shares are lower as investors are concerned the PBOC could hike the reserve requirement ratio or the benchmark interest rate (in the coming days) to curb inflation after suspending the 3-year bill sale. The Shanghai Composite Index is down 0.3% at 2841.35 and it's tipped to hover around current level for the rest of the session. "The Shanghai index could rebound next week if the central bank doesn't launch any (additional tightening) measures after the November data," says Li Lei at Gold State Securities. Among most active stocks, China Vanke (000002.SZ) down 1.3% at CNY8.38, Poly Real Estate Group (600048,SH) down 1.7% at CNY12.49, China Everbright Bank (601818.SH) down 1.6% at CNY3.73. Shenzhen index is down 0.7% at 1296.49. (wynne.wang@dowjones.com)

0200 GMT [Dow Jones] Taiwan shares are +0.9% at 8779.54, after consolidating for the past 2 days, on strength in semiconductors and financials; resistance is tipped at 8800. "The recent upside is faster than we expected ... retail margins have been the highest since the debt crisis, so December's been a strong month. But typically when you have a good December you see a pull back in January," says Yuanta head
Page 153 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
of research John Brebeck. Adds may be premature for the market to sustain the 8800-8900 level. Fubon (2881.TW) is off 2.7% at NT$37.20 after ING announces the sale of NT$15.90 billion of Fubon shares, Cathay Financial (2882.TW) is +0.7% at NT$47.55, TSMC (2330.TW) is +2.8% at NT$69.90, UMC (2303.TW) is +2.5% at NT$16.50 and Acer (2353.TW) is +0.6% at NT$98.70. WC     1,696 words

0240 GMT [Dow Jones] Crude oil climbs in early Asia trading as USD weakens while optimistic views over fundamentals persist. The ICE Dollar Index is down 0.258 at 79.750 with robust Australia jobs data triggering EUR-buying as investors turn to riskier assets; also, product inventories' gains in the latest EIA report are being interpreted as seasonal, "a sort of obligatory round of moves by refineries as the year ends," advisory firm Cameron Hanover says in a research note. Market players are still expecting Friday's monthly IEA and OPEC reports to show sizable upward demand revisions, says Ritterbusch and Associates. January Nymex crude was last up 79 cents at 89.07/bbl.(max.lin@dowjones.com)

TD
0233 GMT [Dow Jones] USD/CNY falls amid an increase in selling interest in the USD; the pair is at
6.6578 vs 6.6617 late yesterday, and is set to keep consolidating in the 6.6500-6.6600 band, says
Shanghai-based trader at foreign bank. Expects selling demand stems from a higher-than-expected
central parity; "the reference rate is not bad, so customers are in a rush to sell the U.S. unit in case the
dollar drops again in coming days." PBOC sets the USD/CNY central parity at 6.6654 vs 6.6616
yesterday. (rose.yu@dowjones.com)

0225 GMT [Dow Jones] Taiwan government bonds are mixed with long-term notes falling on weaker U.S. Treasurys, says local brokerage trader. 30-year government bond starts when-issued trade today; yield last at 2.0550% vs 2.0200% at open. 10-year yield is steady at 1.4535% in when-issued trade as traders stay on the sidelines ahead of reopened 10-year bond auction (to start midday). Expects the 10-year
bond yield in 1.4400%-1.4800% band at the auction. Still, another local bank trader tips the 10-year bond yield in 1.4200%-1.4500% band; "Chunghwa Post and insurers are likely to buy 10-year bonds below
1.4500%," he says. Adds, Chunghwa Post, the island's largest bond player, bought the 10-year bond aggressively around 1.4500% yesterday. 5-year yield is tad lower at 1.0000% vs 1.0050% yesterday. (mason.wu@dowjones.com)

HD      MARKET TALK: Korea Bonds Mixed; Eyes On BOK Gov Comments
WC     1,766 words
PD      9 December 2010
ET       03:44 AM
SN      Dow Jones Global FX & Fixed Income News
SC      CM
LA       English
CY      © 2010 Dow Jones & Company, Inc.
