TD
0244 GMT [Dow Jones] Korea bonds are mixed, with BOK's comments in statement earlier that geopolitical risks in Korea are a downside risk for the economy helping some tenors and bond futures rise, participants say. Note, 3-year bonds are weak on expectations the government may act to resolve a recent supply shortage for those bonds; the 3-year yield is quoted +6 bps at 3.14%, the 5-year yield is down 2 bps at 3.93%, the 10-year yield is down 1 bp at 4.36% while the 20-year yield is flat at 4.55%. December futures are up 14 ticks as foreigners net buy more than 5,000 contracts so far. "We'll have to
see what the BOK governor has to say about geopolitical concerns," says Taurus Investment & Securities analyst Kong Dong-rak. But adds "I don't think the risks relating to North Korea are big enough to dent the BOK's current stance of normalizing the key policy rate" at a measured and moderate pace.
(min-jeong.lee@dowjones.com)

0241 GMT [Dow Jones] HSI +0.6% at 23,228.97, supported by modest rise on Wall Street, but gains are likely capped amid continued concerns over possible further tightening in China, especially given that China bourses are mixed today with Shanghai Composite last down 0.02% at 2847.89. Resistance is tipped at early high of 23,269.36. "The rate hike overhang may continue to drag China stocks until a move is confirmed by the PBOC," says Haitong. Adds, measures to filter capital inflow should prove
overdone in view of the poor performance of the mainland bourses so far this year, while sentiment in the local market has also been cautious. House expects better buying momentum in HK retailing operators and HK property investors as investors stay away from China stocks that are more vulnerable to policy changes. HSBC (0005.HK) +1.1% at HK$80.95 after rally in U.S. financial stocks, while China Resources Land (1109.HK) is down 0.3% at HK$13.82 on rate hike concerns in China. Volume is modest at HK$12.83 billion. (susanna.tai@dowjones.com)

HD       Government concerned over EU flat panel fines
BY       (By Lin Shu-yuan, Ho Meng-kuei, Hsieh Jiun-wei and Deborah Kuo)
WC      487 words
PD       9 December 2010
SN       Central News Agency English News
SC       CNAENG
LA        English
CY       (c) 2010 All materials contained on this site may not be reproduced, distributed, transmitted, displayed, published or broadcast without the prior written permission of the Central News Agency.

LP
Taipei, Dec. 9 (CNA) The government expressed concern Thursday over heavy fines the European     Commission has slapped on four Taiwanese flat panel makers for alleged price-fixing.

Minister of Economic Affairs Shih Yen-shiang said the government will provide any assistance necessary if the fined companies ask for help.

TD
Shih said, however, that the government should have confidence in the companies' ability to deal with international lawsuits, as all of them have multinational operations and have their own legal teams.

In July last year, the  European Commission -- the European Union's top decision-maker -- brought charges against Chi Mei Optoelectronics Corp., AU Optronics Corp. (AUO) , Chunghwa Picture Tubes Ltd. and HannStar Display Corp., along with LG Display of South Korea, accusing them of price-fixing.

Samsung Electronics, the world's largest flat panel maker, was not charged, since it blew the whistle to the European Commission on the price-fixing.

The EU antitrust regulator accused the firms of violating EU law through a conspiracy to engage in unfair price-fixing  practices to hurt flat panel buyers in the production of products such as computers, mobile phones, TVs, digital watches and MP3 players.

The European Commission issued its decision Wednesday against the five manufacturers, which could face combined total fines to the tune of 649 million euros (US$862 million).

Of the five, Chi Mei -- which merged with Innolux Display Corp. to form Chimei Innolux Corp. in March -- received the heaviest penalty, with a  fine of 300 million euros.

Meanwhile, Sun Li-chun, a commissioner with the Cabinet-level Fair Trade Commission, said the agency is willing to extend a helping hand if the government is allowed to intervene.

Sun noted that based on past experience, the amounts of that  fines are negotiable if the accused companies appeal and explain their situations.
AUO, which was  fined 116.8 million euros, has already said it will appeal.

An AUO spokesman said it has cooperated with the EU authorities over the past four years in their investigation into industry practices regarding the production and marketing of TFT-LCD products.

Meanwhile, Council for Economic Planning and Development (CEPD) Chairwoman Christina Liu also said the government will try its best to help if the four companies ask.

Liu attributed the EU move -- a repetition of a similar antitrust case in the United States -- in part to the economic downturn in Europe and the U.S.

"These two areas tend to take more aggressive approaches when their economies are not in good shape," she said.


Page 161 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
Chi Mei and Chunghwa said they will examine the EU decision more closely before taking their next steps. A Chi Mei executive said the 300 million-euro  fine is "really too harsh."
Chunghua was fined 9 million euros, while HannStar got a  fine of 8.1 million euros.

HD     'EC fines LCD makers EUR 649 mln for cartel forming' WC    196 words
PD     9 December 2010
SN     DMEurope
SC     DMEUR
LA     English
CY     © 2010 DMEurope. All rights reserved.

LP
The European Commission has fined six LCD panel producers a total of EUR 648.83 million for operating a cartel which harmed European buyers of television sets, computers and other products that use LCD components. The six are Samsung Electronics and LG Display of Korea and Taiwanese firms AU Optronics, Chimei InnoLux, Chunghwa Picture Tubes and HannStar Display. Samsung Electronics received full immunity from fines under the commission's leniency programme, as it was the first to provide information about the cartel. The cartel operated between October 2001 and February 2006. During the four years, the companies agreed prices, including price ranges and minimum prices, exchanged information on future production planning, capacity utilisation, pricing and other commercial conditions. The  cartel members held monthly multilateral meetings and further bilateral meetings. In total they met around 60 times mainly in hotels in Taiwan for what they called "the Crystal meetings".

TD
The investigation by the commission shows that the companies were aware they were breaking competition rules and took steps to conceal the venue and results of the meetings.

CHARTING THE SENSEX
The Bombay Stock Exchange's 30-share Sensitive Index could rise to 19,760, according to charts.

TD
But Sensex has to move past major resistance at 19,850 to impart momentum to the short-term uptrend.

Until the index moves past 19,850, it would be vulnerable to a test of minor support 19,590. A fall below major support at 19,300 would indicate a reversal of the short-term bullish trend.
The National Stock Exchange's 50-share Nifty may test resistance at 5,930.

A rise above major resistance at 5,945 would lend momentum to the short-term bullish trend. While minor is at 5,885, a drop below major support at 5,850 would lend momentum to the downtrend.




US STOCKS
U.S. shares ended higher Wednesday, as surging financial stocks more than offset a broad decline across the market.

The U.S. dollar continued its recent run higher, pushing down prices of some commodities and hitting the stocks of materials, energy and industrial companies.


Page 164 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
Consumer-discretionary stocks also finished lower, weighed by a 2% decline in McDonald's. The fast-food chain led declines among Dow components after reporting same-store sales rose 4.8% in November, but fell short of analysts' estimates.

Pulling on the other side were financial stocks, fueled by gains at smaller regional banks. Lincoln National jumped 7.5%, Fifth Third Bancorp surged 6.5%, and Zions Bancorp added 5.5%. Regions Financial, Keycorp and PNC Financial Services all gained between 2.9% and 5.3%.

Morgan Stanley rose 3.2%, after the consortium of investors buying the investment bank's 34.3% stake in China International Capital all won their necessary approvals. Bank of America surged 3.7% to lead the Dow, while J.P. Morgan Chase added 2.6%.

But American International Group tumbled 3.9%, after The Wall Street Journal reported that the U.S. government is looking to sell at least $15 billion of its shares in the insurer in the first of several stock offerings to investors starting in early 2011.




ASIAN STOCKS
Asian stock markets were mostly higher Thursday, with shares in Sydney powering to a four-week high after a strong employment report while the Tokyo market continued to benefit from a lower yen.
Japan's Nikkei Stock Average, Australia's S&P/ASX 200 and South Korea's Kospi Composite were all
up while New Zealand's NZX-50 was flat. Dow Jones Industrial Average futures were 52 points higher in
screen trade.

A positive finish for U.S. stocks Wednesday aided regional sentiment, with fianancial stocks rising on the back of gains in their peers on Wall Street.

Mitsubishi UFJ FG rose 2.0% and Sumitomo Mitsui FG advanced 1.9% in Tokyo, while in Sydney ANZ Bank added 1.0% and Westpac Bank climbed 1.7%, and KB Financial Group added 0.3% and Shinhan Financial Group tacked on 0.4% in Seoul.

In Sydney, the market received a boost from a strong employment report with the benchmark S&P/ASX Index tapping a four-week high of 4747.1
Apart from banking stocks, resources were also higher. BHP Billiton rose 0.9% and Fortescue was 1.2%
higher.
In Japan, Kyocera rose 1.5%, Sony added 1.0% and Honda Motor advanced 1.1%.

In Seoul, financial and tech plays underpinned early gains. LG Display added 0.3%, reversing earlier losses that were driven by news the  European Commission had imposed a EUR215 million  fine for price fixing  between 2001-2006.
Samsung Electronics rose 0.5% and Hynix Semiconductor added 0.6%.

The Bank of Korea's decision to hold rates steady at 2.50%, as expected, didn't have any notable impact on the market.


FOREX
The euro was fetching $1.3299, from $1.3261 late Wednesday in New York, and at Y111.37 against the yen, from Y111.44. The dollar was at Y83.80, from Y84.03.


METALS
Gold futures fell Wednesday, with investors cashing in on record prices as they mulled the longer-term inflation and interest rate implications of extended U.S. tax cuts.
Spot gold was at $1,385.20 per troy ounce, up $3.90 from its New York close Wednesday.

Base metals closed mostly higher on the London Metal Exchange Wednesday after improving demand prospects stemmed the impact of a firmer U.S. dollar.

HD      ANTI-TRUST POLICY : LCD PANEL CARTEL FINED 648 MN EURO WC     372 words
PD      9 December 2010
SN      Europolitics SC      EURREP VOL    4100
LA      English
CY      Copyright 2010 Europe Information Service All Rights Reserved

LP
The European Commission fined six manufacturers of liquid crystal display (LCD) panels a total of
€648,925,000, on 8 December, for operating a  cartel. The decision brings to a close an investigation
launched last July following a number of complaints.
The world's second and third largest  LCD panel manufacturers were  fined nearly two-thirds of the total.

TD
LCD panels are the main component of flat screens used in televisions, computer monitors and electronic notebooks.

The firms concerned are Korean - Samsung Electronics and LG Display (numbers one and two worldwide, respectively) - and Taiwanese - AU Optronics (number three worldwide), Chimei Innolux Corporation (second largest national manufacturer), Chunghwa Picture Tubes and HannStar Display Corporation. However, since they trade in the European Economic Area (EEA), "they must play fair," said Competition Commissioner Joaquín Almunia. "The fact that they are foreign companies is no excuse. The companies in question knew they were breaking competition rules and took steps to conceal their illegal behaviour," he added.

They met around 60 times between October 2001 and February 2006, mostly in hotels in Taiwan, for what they called the Crystal meetings', explained the EU executive. They agreed price ranges and minimum prices and exchanged information on future production planning, capacity utilisation and other commercial conditions. The impact on consumers in the EEA was direct because the great majority of televisions, computer screens and notebooks using  LCD panels and sold in the EEA are made in Asia.

The amount of the  fines takes account of sales of the products concerned in the EEA, the very serious nature of the infringement, its geographical scope (EEA) and its duration. Samsung Electronics was given full immunity under the Commission's 2002 leniency programme because it blew the whistle and provided valuable information to the Commission to prove the infringement. None of the companies met the conditions for a reduction of the  fine because of inability to pay.
The fines (in euro):
Samsung: 0 (100% reduction)
LG Display: 215million (50% reduction and partial immunity for 2006) AU Optronics: 116.8 million
Chimei Innolux Corporation: 300 million (20% reduction) Chunghwa Picture Tubes: 9.025 million (5% reduction)
HannStar Display Corporation: 8.1 million

Page 171 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.



SE         COMPANIES - INTERNATIONAL
HD        Display panel cartel fined €649m
BY         By Nikki Tait in Brussels
WC        427 words
PD         9 December 2010
SN         Financial Times
SC         FTFT
ED         Asia Ed1
PG        16
LA         English
CY         Copyright 2010 The Financial Times Ltd. All rights reserved. Please do not cut and paste FT articles and redistribute by email or post to the web.

LP
electronic equipment

Five Taiwanese and South Korean electronics companies in a  cartel with Samsung have been  fined a total of €648.9m ($858m) by Europe's antitrust watchdog. The companies ran their operation in the market for display panels that are used in consumer gadgets.

TD
The five companies are SamsungLG Display of South Korea and Taiwan's AU Optronics, Chimei
Innolux, Chunghwa Picture Tubes and HannStar Display.
Samsung blew the whistle on the  cartel and so escaped penalty.

EU officials said on Wednesday that the companies met more than 60 times over about four years to agree prices, production schedules and other commercial conditions.

The assignations, called "the crystal meetings", took place mainly in Taiwanese hotels, but had a big knock-on effect in Europe, where large volumes of televisions, computer monitors and notebooks using the panels were sold.

The biggest single penalty will be paid by Chimei, at €300m. LG Display faces a €215m  fine, but this came after significant reductions because the company co-operated and was the first to produce evidence that the  cartel continued beyond 2005. It received partial immunity.

Of the other three companies, AU Optronics is  fined €116.8m, after getting a 20 per cent reduction for co-operation; Chunghwa pays €9.025m after a 5 per cent reduction for co-operation; and HannStar is fined €8.1m.

Joaquín Almunia, EU competition commissioner, said the case showed that "foreign companies, like European ones, need to understand that if they want to do business in Europe they must play fair". "The companies concerned knew that they were breaking competition rules and took steps to conceal their illegal behaviour."

He added that two of the companies, who remain unidentified, had asked for reductions in  fines on grounds of financial hardship and "inability to pay," but that these arguments did not succeed.
In similar probes into the  LCD market in the US and Japan, Japanese companies were also penalised. Mr Almunia said that there had been no proof that their products were involved in the particular markets
that were examined by the  European Commission, which included thin-film  LCD panels used in
computers, mobile phones, TVs, digital watches, pocket calculators and MP3 players.




Page 172 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
This is the seventh  cartel case dealt with by Brussels this year, and takes the total amount of  fines to in excess of €3bn. The record annual total was in 2007 when  fines topped €3.3bn on aggregate. Between
2006 and 2010 fines have exceeded €1.5bn a year.

Sour BlackBerrys?

Research In Motion shares slid for a second day in a row on North American stock markets, as the stock gave back the gains they achieved earlier this month.

TD
RIM shares closed at $62 in Toronto, down 72 cents for the day and down from $63.85 at Monday's close. In New York, the shares slipped 75 cents to close at $61.37 US. That's down three per cent from
$63.33 on Monday.

RIM co-chief executive Mike Lazaridis said Tuesday that some of the PlayBook's advanced features will be included in future BlackBerry smartphones. But Lazaridis said he disagreed with a perception that
the BlackBerry smartphones are out-of-date, saying they're aimed at a global market where many carriers have second-generation wireless networks.

Fines for LCD price-fixing

The European Commission imposed fines Wednesday on five South Korean and Taiwanese companies for fixing  the prices of liquid-crystal display panels in popular devices such as flat-screen televisions, computers and notebook devices. The  fines, totalling 649 million euro or $859.6 million US, were related to violations dating to 2001, when the companies started meeting to fix prices of  LCD screens.
Pro-oilsands ad campaign

A U.S. energy industry lobby group is planning a media blitz to counter negative publicity over plans for a controversial pipeline to transport Alberta oilsands crude to the Gulf coast.
The American Petroleum Institute plans to unveil its ad campaign in January.

Cindy Schild, the API's manager of downstream and industry operations, says the ads will promote the economic benefits and jobs that oilsands crude will bring to the U.S.

The move comes just a day after an environmental coalition said it planned a half-million-dollar ad campaign against TransCanada Corporation's proposed Keystone XL project.
AIG to pay off massive loan

Bailed-out insurance conglomerate American International Group Inc. is taking a key step toward paying off a bailout that was at one point worth $182 billion US - the largest of the financial crisis.

The company says in a public filing Wednesday that it will pay off a loan from the Federal Reserve Bank of New York. AIG says that will clear the way for the United States Treasury to sell off the government's stake.

Home Depot ups estimate

ATLANTA Home Depot Inc. is raising its fiscal 2010 earnings-per-share guidance for the second time in two months as North Americans begin to take on more home-improvement projects.
The retail giant now expects net income from continuing operations to be $1.97 per share. That's up
from prior guidance of $1.94 per share. The company now expects revenue to rise 2.3 per cent, up from
the 2.2 per cent rise expected previously, implying revenue of $67.7 billion.
Dollarama on growth spree

MONTREAL Dollarama will accelerate store expansion next year, particularly in Western Canada as the retailer continues to build the leading Canadian discount chain.
The company plans to add 50 stores in 2011 with one-third to 40 per cent of the growth being focused in
Western Canada.
That follows some 45 stores added in the past year, mostly in Ontario. Costco income jumps in Q1
PORTLAND, Ore. Costco Wholesale Corp. said its first-quarter net income rose 17 per cent - even faster than revenue - with help from higher gas prices and rising sales of high-profit items.

SE         finance
HD         E.U. levies fines on screen makers; Korean companies cited for operating a cartel in flat-panel display  market
BY         BY JAMES KANTER
WC        439 words
PD         9 December 2010
SN         International Herald Tribune
SC         INHT
PG         16
LA          English
CY         © 2010 The New York Times Company. All Rights Reserved.

LP
The European Commission slapped fines totaling €649 million on five South Korean and Taiwan companies on Wednesday for  fixing  the prices of liquid crystal display panels in popular devices like flat-screen televisions, computers and notebook devices.

Although most of the price-fixing  meetings took place in Taiwan, the Brussels regulator said the  fines, equivalent to $858 million, were necessary because the activities of the companies raised prices on goods with a value of more than €7 billion sold to European consumers.

TD
‘‘Foreign companies, like European ones, have an obligation to respect competition rules when they do business in Europe,’’ Joaquín Almunia, the E.U. competition commissioner, said at a news conference.
‘‘The fact that the  cartel meetings took place outside the E.U. is no excuse,’’ he said.

Chimei Innolux, a Taiwan company, must pay €300 million, the largest amount. The other Taiwan companies that received  fines were AU Optronics, Chunghwa Picture Tubes and HannStar Display.

Samsung Electronics of Korea escaped without a  fine because it reported the  cartel to the authorities in the first place.
A second Korean company, LG Display, was  fined €215 million, the second-largest amount.
Mr. Almunia said the six manufacturers met about 60 times between 2001 and 2006 to agree on prices
— including price ranges and minimum prices — and to exchange information on future production
planning, capacity utilization and trading conditions.

‘‘This was a very well organized  cartel with monthly meetings, called ‘the crystal meetings,’ held mostly in hotels in Taiwan,’’ he said.

The group fixed the prices of  LCD panels that were sold either alone or already as part of televisions, computers and notebook devices.

The commission has imposed  fines totaling €3.1 billion this year in  cartel cases, the second highest year on record. The record was set in 2007, when the commission imposed  fines totaling €3.3 billion.

Money paid by offenders in E.U.  cartel cases helps to offset contributions by governments to the central E.U. budget, which pays for things like the Common Agricultural Policy and development aid to poorer regions.

Mr. Almunia also announced on Wednesday that he had dropped antitrust charges against Visa Europe, a card payments company, after accepting its pledge to cut fees passed on to retailers for cross-border transactions.

Visa Europe said it was in talks on ‘‘reaching an agreed outcome’’ on a separate investigation into fees for credit-card and deferred-debit transactions, where customers must settle their bills at the end of the month.

The European Commission imposed fines Wednesday on five South Korean and Taiwanese companies for fixing  the prices of liquid crystal display panels in popular devices like flat-screen televisions, computers and notebook devices.

The fines, totaling €649 million, or $857 million, were related to violations dating back to 2001, when the companies started meeting to fix prices of  LCD screens.

TD
Although most of the illegal activity took place in Taiwan, the Brussels regulator said European action was necessary because the activities of the companies raised prices on goods sold to European consumers. The value of the goods was more than €7 billion, the commission said.

‘‘Foreign companies, like European ones, have an obligation to respect competition rules when they do business in Europe,’’ the E.U. competition commissioner, Joaquín Almunia, told a news conference.
‘‘The fact that the  cartel meetings took place outside the E.U. is no excuse.’’

Chimei Innolux, a Taiwanese company, was ordered to pay €300 million, the largest  fine. The other Taiwanese companies receiving  fines were AU Optronics, Chunghwa Picture Tubes and HannStar Display.

Samsung of South Korea, the largest maker of  LCD screens in the world, was not  fined because it reported the  cartel to the authorities.
A second South Korean company, LG Display, was  fined €215 million, the second-largest amount.
Mr. Almunia said the six manufacturers met about 60 times between 2001 and 2006 to agree on prices
— including price ranges and minimum prices — and to exchange information on future production
planning, capacity utilization, and trading conditions.

‘‘This was a very well organized  cartel with monthly meetings, called ‘the crystal meetings,’ held mostly in hotels in Taiwan,’’ he said.

The cartel fixed the prices of  LCD panels that were sold either alone or as part of televisions, computers and notebook devices.
Money paid by offenders in E.U.  cartel cases helps to offset contributions by governments to the
central E.U. budget, which pays for policies like the Common Agricultural Policy and development aid to
poorer regions.

Mr. Almunia also announced Wednesday that he had dropped antitrust charges against Visa Europe, a card payments company, after accepting its pledge to cut fees passed on to retailers for cross-border transactions.

HD            Corporate  News: LCD Makers Fined Over Alleged  Cartel
BY             By Carolyn Henson
WC           356 words
PD            9 December 2010
SN            The Wall Street Journal
SC            J
PG            B3
LA             English
CY            (Copyright (c) 2010, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.)

LP
BRUSSELS -- The  European Commission on Wednesday fined six makers of liquid-crystal display screens a total of 649 million euros ($861 million) for allegedly operating a  cartel over five years.

The commission, the European Union's executive arm, said Samsung Electronics Co. and LG Display Co. of South Korea and Taiwanese producers AU Optronics Corp., Chimei InnoLux Corp., Chunghwa Picture Tubes and HannStar Display Corp. met monthly in Taiwanese hotels from 2001 to 2006 to agree on prices and share commercially sensitive information.

TD
The commission said LG Display was  fined 215 million euros, AU Optronics 117 million euros, Chimei InnoLux 300 million euros, Chungwa 9 million euros and HannStar 8 million euros. Samsung Electronics got full immunity from the  fines for blowing the whistle on the  cartel.

The fines took into account each company's share of the more than 7 billion euros in  LCD sales in Europe over the  cartel period, the commission said. But it reduced the  fines of some of the companies to reward their cooperation with the investigation.

The EU has the power to  fine companies as much as 10% of their global revenue for breaking its antitrust rules.

The EU's action comes two years after LG Display paid a $400 million  fine and pleaded guilty to criminal price-fixing  charges in the U.S. Chunghwa Picture Tubes pleaded guilty in the same U.S. investigation.
Representatives of the companies weren't available to comment Wednesday.

The LCD makers fined by the EU knew their actions were illegal and took steps to conceal their gatherings, which they called "the crystal meetings," said EU Competition Commissioner Joaquin Almunia. There were around 60 such meetings in all, the commissioner said.

He added that a  cartel document asked all the participants "to take care of confidentiality matters and to limit written communication."

"Foreign companies, like European ones, have the obligation to respect competition rules when they do business in Europe," Mr. Almunia said.
Liquid crystal display screens are used in televisions, computer monitors and laptops.

LG Display is considering filing an appeal on the European Commission’s decision to slap huge  fines on the South Korean company for having participated in a price-fixing  scheme for liquid crystal display (LCD) panels.
LG was fined more than 323 billion won by the  European Commission on Wednesday for violating
European Union laws on fair competition.

TD
The company promised to take responsibility for past inappropriate acts and to pursue more transparent and fairer business practices in the future.

However, LG said that after a careful review, if it appears that there were problems in the commission’s investigation process, LG may lodge an appeal.

LG’s compatriot company Samsung Electronics was also targeted by the  European Commission for price-fixing.  But Samsung has been exempted from  fines, since it voluntarily admitted to its fault and reported it to the  European Commission.

HD                   2 LCD giants face contrasting fates

By Kim Yoo-chul
LG Display, the world's second-biggest  LCD maker, is considering appealing against a fine of
215 million euros ($285 million), levied by the  European Commission (EC) for a price-fixing
scheme.

TD
``We may take the  fine imposition to the General Court in the commission upon review of the situation,’’ said an LG Display spokesman Sohn Young-june, Thursday.
LG’s rival, Samsung was also involved in the  cartel but volunteered to report the scheme to the
European authorities and received no penalty in return.
The official remarks come after European Union (EU) regulators charged LG with breaching EU
laws on restrictive business practices in July, last year.

The EC told LG to pay some $285 million for  fixing  prices of LCD panels with five other firms between 2001 and 2006.

The European regulators claimed the  cartel members held monthly multilateral meetings and further bilateral meetings.

In total, they met around 60 times mainly in hotels in Taiwan for what they called ``the crystal meetings.’’

Samsung Electronics and LG Display are the industry’s two biggest vendors of  LCD panels, shipping parts to almost all technology companies including Apple, Dell and Hewlett-Packard (HP).

LG’s Sohn said he expects the amount of the  fine to be cut as the company is planning to fully cooperate with the EC and added it will strengthen transparency in management by implementing some needed reform measures.

``The decision will not hurt the relationships with our bigger clients. We will keep up our work to supply value-added products to them,’’ the spokesman said.
Despite the levies, LG Display rose by 1.99 percent to end at 41,050 won per share on the
KOSPI, Korea Exchange (KRX), the bourse operator, said.

Market analysts say the  fine will just be a ``one-time event’’ as it was widely anticipated and expects operating profit to rise from the first quarter of next year.

``The EC’s decision will cause a shortcoming. LG Display will fall to rock bottom from the fourth quarter and its share corrections are giving good chances for investors to buy,’’ said Park Hyun, an analyst at Hanwha Securities, in a note to clients.

``LG will suffer from a 544.4 billion won operating loss in the fourth quarter hit by the industry’s bearish mood, however, the amount will decrease to 55.8 billion won in the first quarter of 2011,’’ added Park.

Page 183 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
Samsung Electronics was also part of the ``price-cartel’’ group.

But Samsung received full immunity from the  fines under the commission’s leniency program as it was the first to provide valuable information on the  cartel to prove the infringements.
Article 101 of the EU Treaty prohibits price-fixing  and other practices restrictive of competition.

``I don’t understand Samsung’s moves against business virtues. Samsung is lacking full prudency. It’s too bad,’’ said a top-ranking industry executive, asking not to be identified.
``Samsung was absolved of any  fines as it blew the whistle on the  cartel,’’ added the executive. Taiwanese LCD makers also blamed Samsung over its willing action to be freed from any
wrongdoings.

Taiwan-based Chi Mei Optoelectronics and three other Taiwanese firms were also  fined. Taiwanese LCD makers have been previously known to take action against Samsung, industry sources said.
Song Cheol-gyu, a Samsung spokesman, declined to comment. Officials at Taiwanese makers weren’t available for comment.
In the U.S. Department of Justice antitrust investigation, eight companies, including LG Display, Chi Mei, Chunghwa Picture Tubes, Sharp and Hitachi Displays, have pleaded guilty and paid more than $890 million in criminal  fines for price-fixing,  in a separate case.

HD          Taiwanese, Korean LCD panel makers hit by massive antitrust fines
BY           Martin williams Martin williams
CR          Kyodo
WC          343 words
PD           9 December 2010
ET           12:20 PM
SN           Kyodo News
SC           KYODO
LA           English
CY           (c) 2010 Kyodo News

LP
TAIPEI, Dec. 9 -- Four Taiwanese liquid crystal display panel manufacturers are preparing to appeal or considering their options Thursday after the European Commission handed out 648.9 million euros in fines to the companies and two Korean rivals for running a cartel between 2001 and 2006.

Taiwan's AU Optronics, Chimei InnoLux Corp, Chunghwa Picture Tubes and HannStar Display Corp and South Korea's LG Display and Samsung Electronics ''knew they were breaking competition rules and took steps to conceal their illegal behavior,'' commission Vice President Joaquin Almunia said in a statement Wednesday.

TD
The cartel representatives organized ''around 60'' monthly strategy sessions in Taiwanese hotels known as the ''Crystal meetings'' where they set prices and price ranges and conferred over other commercial conditions.
The regulator said the  cartel members ''took steps to conceal the venue and results of the meetings.'' Chimei InnoLux, which underwent a merger in March well after the offenses took place, had the
heaviest hit of 300 million euros, while AU Optronics was  fined 116.8 million euros, including a 20
percent fine reduction for cooperating with the commission.

Chunghwa Picture Tubes and HannStar Display received smaller  fines of 9 million euros and 8.1 million euros.

The commission cut LG Display's  fine in half to 215 million euros for cooperating with the probe and awarded it immunity for the 2006 portion of the  cartel's operations for providing evidence of the last months of its operations.

Samsung was technically  fined but given full immunity ''as it brought the  cartel to the Commission's attention and provided valuable information to prove the infringement,'' the statement said.

Of the Taiwanese companies, AU Optronics has already indicated it will appeal the  fine, local media reported.

AU Optronics is also facing difficulties in California, where the U.S. District Court in San Francisco has ordered several executives to remain in that state and confiscated their passports ahead of proceedings this week over possible antitrust violations.

CHARTING THE SENSEX
The Bombay Stock Exchange's 30-share Sensitive Index could rise to 19,760, according to charts.

TD
But Sensex has to move past major resistance at 19,850 to impart momentum to the short-term uptrend.

Until the index moves past 19,850, it would be vulnerable to a test of minor support 19,590. A fall below major support at 19,300 would indicate a reversal of the short-term bullish trend.
The National Stock Exchange's 50-share Nifty may test resistance at 5,930.

A rise above major resistance at 5,945 would lend momentum to the short-term bullish trend. While minor is at 5,885, a drop below major support at 5,850 would lend momentum to the downtrend.




US STOCKS
U.S. shares ended higher Wednesday, as surging financial stocks more than offset a broad decline across the market.

The U.S. dollar continued its recent run higher, pushing down prices of some commodities and hitting the stocks of materials, energy and industrial companies.


Page 191 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
Consumer-discretionary stocks also finished lower, weighed by a 2% decline in McDonald's. The fast-food chain led declines among Dow components after reporting same-store sales rose 4.8% in November, but fell short of analysts' estimates.

Pulling on the other side were financial stocks, fueled by gains at smaller regional banks. Lincoln National jumped 7.5%, Fifth Third Bancorp surged 6.5%, and Zions Bancorp added 5.5%. Regions Financial, Keycorp and PNC Financial Services all gained between 2.9% and 5.3%.

Morgan Stanley rose 3.2%, after the consortium of investors buying the investment bank's 34.3% stake in China International Capital all won their necessary approvals. Bank of America surged 3.7% to lead the Dow, while J.P. Morgan Chase added 2.6%.

But American International Group tumbled 3.9%, after The Wall Street Journal reported that the U.S. government is looking to sell at least $15 billion of its shares in the insurer in the first of several stock offerings to investors starting in early 2011.




ASIAN STOCKS
Asian stock markets were mostly higher Thursday, with shares in Sydney powering to a four-week high after a strong employment report while the Tokyo market continued to benefit from a lower yen.
Japan's Nikkei Stock Average, Australia's S&P/ASX 200 and South Korea's Kospi Composite were all
up while New Zealand's NZX-50 was flat. Dow Jones Industrial Average futures were 52 points higher in
screen trade.

A positive finish for U.S. stocks Wednesday aided regional sentiment, with fianancial stocks rising on the back of gains in their peers on Wall Street.

Mitsubishi UFJ FG rose 2.0% and Sumitomo Mitsui FG advanced 1.9% in Tokyo, while in Sydney ANZ Bank added 1.0% and Westpac Bank climbed 1.7%, and KB Financial Group added 0.3% and Shinhan Financial Group tacked on 0.4% in Seoul.

In Sydney, the market received a boost from a strong employment report with the benchmark S&P/ASX Index tapping a four-week high of 4747.1
Apart from banking stocks, resources were also higher. BHP Billiton rose 0.9% and Fortescue was 1.2%
higher.
In Japan, Kyocera rose 1.5%, Sony added 1.0% and Honda Motor advanced 1.1%.

In Seoul, financial and tech plays underpinned early gains. LG Display added 0.3%, reversing earlier losses that were driven by news the  European Commission had imposed a EUR215 million  fine for price fixing  between 2001-2006.
Samsung Electronics rose 0.5% and Hynix Semiconductor added 0.6%.

The Bank of Korea's decision to hold rates steady at 2.50%, as expected, didn't have any notable impact on the market.


FOREX
The euro was fetching $1.3299, from $1.3261 late Wednesday in New York, and at Y111.37 against the yen, from Y111.44. The dollar was at Y83.80, from Y84.03.


METALS
Gold futures fell Wednesday, with investors cashing in on record prices as they mulled the longer-term inflation and interest rate implications of extended U.S. tax cuts.
Spot gold was at $1,385.20 per troy ounce, up $3.90 from its New York close Wednesday.

Base metals closed mostly higher on the London Metal Exchange Wednesday after improving demand prospects stemmed the impact of a firmer U.S. dollar.

SE           Business/Financial Desk; SECTB
HD            Fines Set in LCD Price Fixing
BY           By JAMES KANTER
WC          389 words
PD           9 December 2010
SN           The New York Times
SC           NYTF
ED           Late Edition - Final
PG           12
LA            English
CY           Copyright 2010 The New York Times Company. All Rights Reserved.

LP
BRUSSELS -- The European Commission imposed fines Wednesday on five South Korean and Taiwanese companies for fixing  the prices of liquid-crystal display panels in popular devices like flat-screen televisions, computers and notebook devices.

The fines, totaling 649 million euros ($859.6 million), were related to violations dating to 2001, when the companies started meeting to fix prices of  LCD screens. Although most of the illegal activity took place in Taiwan, the Brussels regulator said European action was necessary because the activities of the companies raised prices on goods sold to European consumers. The value of the goods was more than 7 billion euros, the commission said.

TD
''Foreign companies, like European ones, have an obligation to respect competition rules when they do business in Europe,'' the European competition commissioner, Joaquin Almunia, told a news conference. ''The fact that the  cartel meetings took place outside the E.U. is no excuse.''

Chimei Innolux, a Taiwanese company, was ordered to pay almost $400 million, the largest  fine. The other Taiwanese companies ordered to pay  fines were AU Optronics, Chunghwa Picture Tubes and HannStar Display.

Samsung of South Korea, the largest maker of  LCD screens in the world, was not  fined because it had reported the  cartel to the authorities.
A second South Korean company, LG Display, was  fined $286 million, the second-largest amount. Mr. Almunia said the six manufacturers met about 60 times from 2001 to 2006 to agree on prices --
including price ranges and minimum prices -- and to exchange information on future production
planning, capacity utilization and trading conditions.

The cartel fixed the prices of  LCD panels that were sold either alone or in televisions, computers and notebook devices.
The commission, the executive agency of the European Union, has imposed  fines totaling more than
$4 billion this year in cartel cases, the second-highest year on record. The record is 2007, when the
commission imposed fines totaling nearly $4.4 billion.

Mr. Almunia also announced Wednesday that he had dropped antitrust charges against Visa Europe, a card payments company, after accepting its pledge to cut fees passed on to retailers for
cross-border transactions.

Visa Europe said it was still in talks on settling a separate inquiry into fees for credit card and deferred debit transactions.

HD        EC fines LCD makers EUR 649 mln for cartel forming
WC       186 words
PD        9 December 2010
SN        Telecompaper Europe
SC        TELEUR
LA        English
CY        Copyright 2010 Telecompaper. All Rights Reserved.

LP
The European Commission has fined six LCD panel producers a total of EUR 648.83 million for operating a cartel which harmed European buyers of television sets, computers and other products that use LCD components. The six are Samsung Electronics and LG Display of Korea and Taiwanese firms AU Optronics, Chimei InnoLux, Chunghwa Picture Tubes and HannStar Display. Samsung Electronics received full immunity from fines under the commission's leniency programme, as it was the first to provide information about the cartel. The cartel operated between October 2001 and February 2006. During the four years, the companies agreed prices, including price ranges and minimum prices, exchanged information on future production planning, capacity utilisation, pricing and other commercial conditions. The  cartel members held monthly multilateral meetings and further bilateral meetings. In total they met around 60 times mainly in hotels in Taiwan for what they called "the Crystal meetings".

TD
The investigation by the commission shows that the companies were aware they were breaking competition rules and took steps to conceal the venue and results of the meetings.

It will be the eighth highest  fine from the fines imposed by the European Commission on groups of firms due to the violation of business competition rules.

HD          Gov't willing to help fined panel makers
BY          The China Post Staff
WC         535 words
PD          10 December 2010
SN          The China Post
SC          CHIPOS
LA          English
CY          (c) 2010 The China Post. All Rights Reserved

LP
The China Post news staff -- The government yesterday expressed its concerns over  fines imposed by the European Union on Taiwan's flat panel makers and said it will do its best to help the firms weather the crisis.
Shih Yen-shiang, Minister of Economic Affairs, yesterday said he has already asked the Industrial
Development Bureau under the ministry to see what help flat panel makers may need at this time.

TD
“The firms have told us that at this point they haven't received the official ruling,” Shih said. “Once they get the ruling we'll find out how the government may help.”

The European Commission Wednesday imposed a total of 433.92 million euros in  fines on four Taiwanese flat panel makers for allegedly engaging in price-fixing.  The four firms were Chimei Innolux, AU Optronics, Chunghwa Picture Tubes and HannStar Display Corp.
The EU accused the four, as well as Korea's Samsung and LG, of colluding to fix prices.

In a news release issued by the EU's fair trade unit, the European Union accused the six of holding over 60 so-called “crystal meetings” from October 2001 to February 2006, discussing how they could work together to keep prices at an advantageous level.

The name “crystal meeting” was taken from the major component of any  LCD panels, namely liquid crystal. The meetings were later exposed to the EU by Samsung, which was not  fined in this case.
Chimei Innolux got the heaviest  fine of 300 million euros among the four companies, while AU was
fined 116.8 million euros, Chunghwa 9.02 million euros, and HannStar. 8.1 million euros.

The fines were issued after the United States imposed similar penalties for the flat panel makers, which form Taiwan's state-of-the-art TFT-LCD industry that churns out products worth well over NT$1 trillion annually.

“This is a learning experience for them. The firms learn fast, and we should have confidence in them,” Shih said, when asked how the flat panel makers should respond to these actions.

He further pointed out powerful, prestigious companies like AU and Chi Mei have their own legal affairs departments that can handle cases like this. “Yet every lawsuit is different, and we will provide all necessary help and assistance,” he said.
Meanwhile, the Cabinet-level Fair Trade Commission (FTC) has also expressed its willingness to help. “We haven't received any requests from the companies asking for help,” said Sun Li-chun, an FTC
member. “Yet FTC will provide all the necessary help within the boundaries of what the government
can do in these situations.”

Currently, only AU Optronics has expressed its resolve to appeal the ruling. “Based on former experiences, the EU is likely to 'reconsider' the penalty if a ruling was appealed,” Sun said.
Separately, shares of Chimei Innolux Corp. closed lower yesterday in the wake of the EU ruling.

Page 200 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
Under-performing the broader market, Chimei Innolux fell 5.32 percent to NT$38.3, while the benchmark weighted index rose 50.05 to 8,753.84.
AUO shares fell 2.44 percent to close at NT$30.05.

SE              Business
HD             LG Display may appeal fine
BY              Kim Ji-hyun (jemmie@heraldm.com)
WC             338 words
PD              10 December 2010
SN              The Korea Herald
SC              KORHER
LA              English
CY              (c) 2010 The Korea Herald

LP
LG Display on Thursday said it was considering appealing against a  fine imposed by the European
Commission for price-fixing.
The Seoul-based company hopes to reduce the amount of  fines through the action.

TD
“LG Display acknowledges the wrongful acts of the past and respects the  European Commission’s regulatory authority in this regard,” the company said in a statement.
“However, LG Display may, after careful review and consideration, appeal (the) decision.”

The appeal will have to be submitted within 60 days of the commission’s ruling, company officials said.
The European Commission on Wednesday fined LG Display 215 million euros ($285 million) for
fixing  the prices of liquid-crystal display panels.
LG was a part of a  cartel with five other firms between 2001-2006, the commission said.

Samsung Electronics, the world’s largest  LCD maker, also took part but escaped  fines because it provided information to the commission about the  cartel.
Rival companies often present such evidence of wrongdoing to authorities to avoid  fines.

“Foreign companies, like European ones, have an obligation to respect competition rules when they do business in Europe, EU Competition Commissioner Joaquin Almunia told reporters in Brussels regarding the ruling, according to Bloomberg.

LCD panels are a central component of the thin, flat monitors used in televisions, computer monitors and laptops.

The five firms sold panels in Europe worth about 7 billion euros during the  cartel, the commission said.
Some of the others in the  cartel have said they would appeal.

Chi Mei, which merged with Innolux Display Corp. in March to form Chimei Innolux Corp., was slapped with the heftiest penalty of 300 million euros. Taiwan’s AU Optronics Corp. must pay a penalty of 116.8 million euros, while Chunghwa Picture Tubes Ltd. ― also of Taiwan ― was  fined 9 million euros. Another Taiwanese firm, HannStar Display Corp., was  fined 8.1 million euros.
LG Display said it had taken comprehensive measures to avoid repetition of such mistakes.

HD      Taiwan says EU price-fixing fines will hurt industry
WC     265 words
PD      11 December 2010
ET       10:05 AM
SN      Agence France Presse
SC      AFPR
LA       English
CY      Copyright Agence France-Presse, 2010 All reproduction and presentation rights reserved.

LP
Taiwan's government said Saturday that huge price-fixing fines imposed by the European Commission
will hurt its flat panel industry and vowed to help local firms affected by the measures.

"The huge  fines will negatively impact our industry," the ministry of economic affairs said in a statement, adding it will meet the firms next week to discuss the  fines.

TD
The European Commission this week slapped fines totalling 649 million euros (860 million dollars) on five Taiwanese flat panel makers and on one South Korean firm.

The leader in the  LCD business, South Korea's Samsung Electronics, was also accused of being part of the cartel but escaped cash sanctions for coming forward first with information on the alleged scheme.
Terry Gou, chairman of Taiwan's IT giant Hon Hai Precision, has vowed to fight back for its affiliate
Chimei Innolux Corporation, which faces the largest  fine of 300 million euros.
Gou also blasted Samsung for turning on other firms in order to escape punishment.

"Is it fair that a repeat offender is found not guilty?... We won't easily pay the money that we should not be paying. We will fight all the way," he told reporters on Friday.

Taiwan's AU Optronics has said it will challenge the  fine while the other Taiwanese firms have said they are considering whether to appeal.

The Commission accused the firms of running a  cartel between October 2001 and February 2006 that fixed prices, harming European buyers of televisions and computers equipped with liquid crystal displays.

HD     Taiwanese tycoon: EU should  have fined Samsung for price fixing  along with rest of cartel
WC    431 words
PD     11 December 2010
ET      07:56 AM
SN     Associated Press Newswires
SC     APRS
LA      English
CY     (c) 2010. The Associated Press. All Rights Reserved.

LP
TAIPEI, Taiwan (AP) - The head of Taiwanese electronics giant Foxconn Technology Group questioned the European Union decision to exempt Samsung Electronics Co. from price-fixing fines for makers of LCD panels, accusing his South Korean rival of being the  cartel's main culprit.

Terry Gou's comments came after the EU competition watchdog  fined South Korea's LG Display and four Taiwanese manufacturers euro649 million ($863 million) Wednesday for  fixing  prices on the flat-screen panels between 2001 and 2006.

TD
Samsung, the world's biggest LCD maker, also participated in the price fixing  but escaped a fine
because it blew the whistle on the cartel, according to the European Commission.

Foxconn does not make  LCD panels, but Gou is a major shareholder of Taiwan's Chimei Innolux Corp., which was fined euro300 million in the case.

Three other Taiwanese makers -- AU Optronics, Chunghwa and HannStar -- were  fined euro116.8 million, euro9 million and euro8.1 million, respectively.
The world's second-biggest  LCD maker, South Korea's LG Display, was  fined euro215 million.
The fines targeted price-fixing  for LCD panels used in flat screens for televisions and computer monitors. Speaking to reporters late Friday, Gou said Samsung and LG Display were leading in the price  fixing,
and Taiwanese makers were only collaborating with them.

"If the No. 1 and No. 2 makers did not lead in  fixing  prices, would Taiwan's No. 3 and No. 4 carry any weight?" he asked.
Gou suggested that Samsung only informed authorities of the improprieties as part of a scheme to beat its
Taiwanese rivals.
South Korean firms "are resorting to all means possible in order to crush us," he said.

Samsung spokesman Jason Kim had no response to Gou's statements when contacted Saturday, saying only "Samsung Electronics respects the EU's decision."

The European Commission said the LCD makers met about 60 times between October 2001 and February 2006, mostly in Taiwanese hotels, for what they called "the Crystal meetings," the commission said. In addition to  fixing  prices, they also exchanged information on their future production plans and other business plans, it said.

The cartel affected  LCD panel sales worth about euro7 billion in the European market, the commission said.

Gou said the EU  fine was levied without giving Chimei a chance to defend itself, noting that the firm will hold its action pending the EU's clarification.
Au Optronics has said it will appeal, while Chunghwa and HannStar have yet to decide what to do.

HD          AU Optronics China plant approved
BY          The China Post Staff
WC         572 words
PD          12 December 2010
SN          The China Post
SC          CHIPOS
LA           English
CY          (c) 2010 The China Post. All Rights Reserved

LP
Premier Wu Den-yih yesterday disclosed that AU Optronics (AUO) has received the greenlight to build an LCD panel plant in China, dismissing complaints that his administration has been dragging its feet screening such investment projects.

Wu said the government's decision-makers have already approved the project, which is now only awaiting the completion of basic paper work at the economics ministry's investment commission.

TD
The premier's revelation was a direct response to a tirade by an angry Terry Gou, chairman of the Hon
Hai Group, over the lack of progress in allowing Taiwan's makers to set up panel factories in China

Gou's anger was triggered by hefty antitrust  fines the European Commission recently imposed on Taiwan's panel makers, including AUO and Chimei Innolux (CMI), in which Hon Hai owns a major stake.

“Why is (the government) tying up Taiwan panel makers,” asked Gou on Friday as he met with economics officials to seek advice over the EU  fines.
Gou, accompanied by Vice Economics Minister Huang Jung-chiou, also went to the EU's trade office in
Taipei to demand an explanation of the  fines.

AUO submitted an application to build an advanced plant in China earlier this year after the Wu administration lifted a ban on Taiwan makers running panel production on the other side of the strait.
But the government later rejected the application, citing a lack of proper papers.
AUO then renewed its application, but the government has yet to give it final approval.

“Chairman Gou must have been away from Taiwan for too long, and he isn't aware of the present progress (of the AUO case),” said Premier Wu.

Wu noted that Taiwan panel makers are only allowed to build fabrication plants in China if the end products are one generation lower than their production in Taiwan in terms of technology. The makers must also promise to keep investing in Taiwan.

AUO has already met both requirements and received the approval without any delay by the government, Wu said, adding CMI has not submitted an application for building panel plants in China.

Commenting on the EU  fines, Wu said he does not know enough to go into detail about the competition between CMI and its competitors.

Business competition between Taiwanese and foreign companies is not something that the government can meddle in, but it will not back off from protecting local companies' rights abroad, the premier said.

The economics ministry said the EU's huge  fines will hurt its  LCD panel industry, but promised help for local firms affected by the antitrust measures.

“The huge fines will negatively impact our industry,” the ministry said in a statement.
Page 209 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
It said it will meet with the firms involved this week to discuss the  fines.

The ministry said it has asked its trade officials in Europe to try to seek an explanation of the case from the European authorities.
Five Taiwanese panel makers and South Korea's LG Display received  fines totaling 649 million euros. But the world's leading  LCD maker, South Korea's Samsung Electronics, escaped punishment,
although it was also charged with playing a part in the price  fixing.
Gou has blasted Samsung for turning on other firms in order to escape punishment.

AUO has vowed to challenge the  fine while the other Taiwanese firms have said they are considering whether to appeal.

HD       Commission fines six LCD panel producers €648 million for fixing cartel
WC      613 words
PD       12 December 2010
SN       New Europe
SC       NEWEU
LA        English
CY       © 2010. New Europe.

LP
The European Commission has fined last week six LCD panel producers a total of €648 925 000 for operating a cartel which harmed European buyers of television sets computers and other products that use the key Liquid Crystal Display component. The six are Samsung Electronics and LG Display of Korea and Taiwanese firms AU Optronics Chimei InnoLux Corporation Chunghwa Picture Tubes and HannStar Display Corporation. Samsung Electronics received full immunity from fines under the Commissions leniency programme as it was the first to provide information about the cartel. Article 101 of the EU Treaty prohibits price-fixing  and other practices restrictive of competition.

TD
Foreign companies like European ones need to understand that if they want to do business in Europe they must play fair. The companies concerned knew they were breaking competition rules and took steps to conceal their illegal behaviour. The only understanding we will show is for those that come forward to denounce a cartel and help prove its existence said Commission Vice President in charge of competition policy Joaquín Almunia.
Last Wednesday the Commission  fined six producers of liquid crystal display LCD panels a total of €648
925 000 for operating a  cartel between October 2001 and February 2006. LCD panels are the main
component of thin flat screens used in televisions computer monitors and electronic notebooks. The
companies are Samsung Electronics and LG Display of Korea and Taiwanese firms AU Optronics
Chimei InnoLux Corporation Chunghwa Picture Tubes and HannStar Display Corporation.

During the four years the companies agreed prices including price ranges and minimum prices exchanged information on future production planning capacity utilisation pricing and other commercial conditions. The  cartel members held monthly multilateral meetings and further bilateral meetings. In total they met around 60 times mainly in hotels in Taiwan for what they called the Crystal meetings.

These agreements had a direct impact on customers in the European Economic Area because the vast majority of televisions computer monitors and notebooks incorporating those  LCD panels and sold in the EEA comes from Asia.
The investigation gathered by the Commission shows that the companies were aware they were
breaking competition rules and took steps to conceal the venue and results of the meetings. A document
requested everybody to take care of security/confidentiality matters and to limit written communication
reminding of the DRAM investigation started in 2002 and concluded in May 2010 see IP/10/586 .

The Commission faced the companies with a Statement of Objections on May 2009 on which they had the opportunity to comment and be heard and after which the Commission reduced the proven duration of the infringement by four months.
The fines

In setting the level of the  fines the Commission took into account the companies sales of the products concerned in the EEA the very serious nature of the infringement its EEA-wide scope and its duration. Samsung Electronics received full immunity under the Commissions 2002 Leniency Notice as it brought the cartel to the Commissions attention and provided valuable information to prove the infringement. The fines of the following undertakings were also reduced for their cooperation with the Commission: LG Display 50% AU Optronics 20% and Chunghwa Picture Tubes 5% . Besides this reduction LG Display also received a full reduction of  fine for its participation in the  cartel in 2006 as it was the first company
Page 211 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
to bring forward evidence showing that the  cartel continued after 2005 so-called partial immunity . None of the companies met the conditions for a reduction of the  fine under paragraph 35 of the Commissions
2006 Guidelines on  Fines inability-to-pay claims . Two had applied.

HD                 AUO nears approval  on investment in Chinese LCD plant; IN A FIX:Officials said they would meet with panel makers next week to discuss how best to respond  to price-fixing allegations in Europe
BY                 By Shih Hsiu-chuan and Kevin Chen
CR                 Staff Reporters
WC                490 words

SC                 TAIP

Premier Wu Den-yih said yesterday that a steering committee of the Investment Commission
under the Ministry of Economic Affairs (MOEA) had agreed to approve AU Optronics Corps (AUO, )
application to invest in a new  LCD panel plant in China.

The review procedure for the case is now focusing on the completion of the regular paperwork, Wu told reporters after Hon Hai Group chairman Terry Gou complained on Friday that the government stands in the way of local flat panel makers plans to invest in China.

TD
It could be that chairman Gou had been out of the country for a long time so that he did not understand the progress of the case, Wu said.

However, the ministrys Investment Commission Executive Secretary Fan Liang-tung said by telephone yesterday that the commission had yet to finalize the review of AU Optronics planned US$3 billion investment in a 7.5-generation  LCD panel plant in Kunshan, Jiangsu Province.

I have no comment on the premiers remark, Fan told the Taipei Times. But what is clear now is that the commission will have to organize an inter--ministerial meeting to formally decide on the case.

The commission usually holds such inter-ministerial meetings once a month and its most recent meeting was held on Nov. 30.

Fan said it was difficult to say when the next such meeting would be held because it involves several government agencies.

AU Optronics, the nations second-largest  LCD panel maker after Chimei Innolux Corp by revenue, submitted its China investment proposal to the commission for approval in March, but had to resubmit the proposal later to meet government requirements.

Wu said the companys revised plan had met the two conditions for the government to decide whether to allow  LCD panel makers to invest in China.

The government only allows Taiwanese companies to set up production lines in China when their locally based panel production has more advanced technologies and when they promise not to scale down investments in Taiwan, he said.
The government did not delay the review of the application, Wu said.

The premier also dismissed Gous criticism that the government did not care about Taiwanese companies being ordered to pay a huge  fine by the European Commission.

The fact that Vice Minister of Economic Affairs Hwang Jung-chiou accompanied Guo and Chimei Innolux chairman Frank Liao to the European Economic and Trade Office on Friday demonstrated the government was concerned about the matter, Wu said.

Five LCD manufacturers were weighing their options at week's end after the European Commission     
fined them $858.8 million for price-fixing.  The Commission issued the  fines late last week, capping a
four-year probe into price-fixing  for LCD panels in Europe. AU Optronics, which was  fined $154.8 million,
and LG Display ($284.5 million) were considering filing an appeal with the general court in Luxembourg.
Chimei Innolux, which plans to recognize a $396.3 million  fine on its Q4 balance sheet, said Friday it was
awaiting a copy of the ruling before deciding on an appeal. The  fine isn't covered by the $235.9 million
Chimei set aside for the case. Chunghwa Picture Tubes and HannStar were  fined $11.9 million and $10.7
million. Nothing was levied against Samsung, which cooperated in the investigation.

HD     Latham & Watkins Picks Up Prominent DOJ Prosecutor
BY     Petra Pasternak
WC    723 words
PD     13 December 2010
SN     The Recorder
SC     RECRDR
PG     19
VOL   Volume 134; Issue 135
LA     English
CY     Copyright 2010 ALM Properties, Inc. All Rights Reserved.

LP
SAN FRANCISCO — Latham & Watkins has bagged prominent antitrust prosecutor Niall Lynch.

Lynch, who's been assistant chief of the Department of Justice's antitrust division in San Francisco for the past five years, will join Latham's San Francisco office as partner on Jan. 10.

TD
Observers say it's a big catch for the firm. Lynch joined the Department of Justice in 1995 from McCutchen, Doyle, Brown & Enersen where he was an associate. During his tenure, he has led or supervised the DOJ's merger, criminal and international  cartel cases.

"Niall is widely viewed as a star in the division, especially in the DRAM and LCD cases," Sheppard, Mullin, Richter & Hampton antitrust lawyer James McGinnis said. Those price-fixing  cases , he said, count
among the biggest and most successful in the antitrust division's history. "I think everyone would regard this as a coup for Latham." McGinnis said Sheppard didn't interview Lynch, citing probable conflicts: McGinnis represents a defendant in an ongoing probe of  LCD flat-panel suppliers. Lynch, speaking from Brussels where he spent the week meeting Latham's European competition lawyers, said he interviewed with at least 10 firms. He said after 15 years with the DOJ he was looking for a change. "I had a real breadth of experience at the Department of Justice," Lynch said. "Now I'm looking for new challenges."

He said his focus at Latham would be global, particularly on price-fixing  cases. Lynch said that last year, the DOJ brought in more than $1 billion in criminal  fines from international  cartel cases, which he expects will continue to be among top priorities.

Lynch said he chose Latham for its global reach, closely woven antitrust team and strong corporate group. "Latham has offices all over the world, which is really essential now in order to deal with cases being defended in five or six countries."

Michael Egge, a co-chairman of Latham's antitrust and competition practice group and a partner in the firm's Washington, D.C., office, said a seamless international antitrust team of lawyers is more important than ever. When the DOJ or the  European Commission open an investigation, it spreads like wildfire, he said. "In a world where a company could get raided in five different countries at once on the very same day, which is what's happening, you want to be able to represent your client by putting people and resources on the ground in all five places at once," he said. "Niall is a huge complement to this."

Conflict rules will prevent Lynch from working on any of his old cases, he said. Latham has represented defendants in DOJ investigations of the global air cargo industry and DRAM memory suppliers. Latham
has about 150 global antitrust and competition lawyers, with about 50 of them in California. San Francisco, Washington, D.C., and Brussels are its biggest antitrust centers.

Lynch said there are six multidistrict litigation cases based in the Northern District of California that originated in the San Francisco office, including SRAM, Flash and optical disc drive-related matters, which he led or supervised. He said those will continue to be handled by the team he oversaw, which includes attorney Michael Scott and Peter Huston, a former Latham partner.

Lynch said the now-closed DRAM investigation led to more than $700 million in criminal  fines and 18 executives charged criminally around the world.

Page 216 of 217 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
With a strong team that includes experienced lawyers like Houston, the DOJ should have no problem moving on after the loss of Lynch, said Sheppard's McGinnis. "I don't think there will even be a hiccup in the ongoing work," McGinnis said. "I think they will transition seamlessly."

And businesses can expect a solid new defender on their side. Berkeley white-collar defense lawyer Cristina Arguedas said there aren't that many people in the region who know the intricacies of antitrust law at Lynch's level of experience who move from the government office into private practice. "He will no
doubt be a tremendous asset to any company that's under investigation," she said. "He has had a lot of power in the position he's held in the government and he used it very effectively and very judiciously."
